Rebuttal of Ibn Kamal Pasha on the Equivalence of Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah
Critical refinement of Ibn Kamal Pasha's distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the established Hanafi position on the synonymity of Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah, and evaluate Ibn Kamal Pasha's deviation from the majority view.

Core Idea
Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah are synonymous; only the six core books constitute Zahir al-Riwayah.

This passage confronts a methodological dispute within the Hanafi school: whether Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah are distinct terms. The Ottoman scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha argued for a distinction, but the established position of the fuqaha rejects any difference. Understanding this is crucial for a mufti to correctly rank sources of authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contested issues
First, Ibn Kamal Pasha distinguishes between Riwayat al-Usul (specific to the six core books) and Zahir al-Riwayah (broader, including rare narrations). Second, he claims Nawadir can become Zahir al-Riwayah without being in the six books. Recognize both claims.
These are two separate but related points.
2
Establish the majority Hanafi view
The text states it is 'firmly established among the jurists (taqarrara 'inda al-fuqaha')' that there is no difference – the terms are synonyms. Furthermore, a Nawadir narration is not considered Zahir al-Riwayah unless mentioned in the books of Usul.
The majority view relies on the consensus (ijma) of the Hanafi jurists.
3
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a mufti follows Ibn Kamal Pasha, he might treat a rare narration (e.g., from al-Muhit) as authoritative as the six core books. The correct view restricts fatwa to the six books, preserving the hierarchy.
This prevents misuse of weaker narrations.

Source Text

مطلب في الرد على العلامة ابن كمال باشا في فرقه بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول ، وفى زعمه أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية بدون ذكرها في كتب الأصول
هذا وقد فرق العلامة ابن كمال باشا (۳) بين رواية الأصول وظاهر الرواية، وزعم أن رواية الأصول خاصة بما في الأمهات الست، وظاهر الرواية عام قد يطلق على ما في غير هذه الستة مما يكون نادر الرواية كرواية الحسن بن زياد في المسألة المذكورة في المحيط و الذخيرة، وكذلك جزم بأن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية من غير أن يكون لها ذكر في كتب ظاهر الرواية، وأنكر العلامة على من صرح بخلافه
(۳) قوله : " وقد فرق العلامة ابن كمال باشا " اعلم أنه قد تقرر عند الفقهاء أنه لا فرق بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول، وأن رواية النوادر لا تكون ظاهر الرواية إلا إذا ذكرت في كتب الأصول، وخالفهم العلامة ابن كمال باشا في المسألتين، فزعم أن رواية الأصول خاصة بما فى الأمهات الست، وظاهر الرواية عام قد يطلق على ما في غير هذه الستة مما يكون نادر الرواية كرواية الحسن بن زياد في المسألة المذكورة في المحيط و الذخيرة، وكذلك جزم بأن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية من غير أن يكون لها ذكر في كتب ظاهر الرواية، وأنكر العلامة على من صرح بخلافه
Section on rebutting the scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha regarding his distinction between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul, and his claim that a narration from al-Nawadir can be considered Zahir al-Riwayah without being mentioned in the books of Usul.
Now, the scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha distinguished between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah. He claimed that Riwayat al-Usul is specific to what is found in the six Ummahat (core books), while Zahir al-Riwayah is general and may be applied to what is outside these six, even if it is a rare narration, such as the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad on the issue mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira. Similarly, he asserted that a narration from al-Nawadir can be considered Zahir al-Riwayah even if it has no mention in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. And the scholar condemned those who explicitly state the contrary.

(3) His saying: 'And the scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha distinguished.' Know that it is firmly established among the jurists that there is no difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul, and that a narration from al-Nawadir is not considered Zahir al-Riwayah unless it is mentioned in the books of Usul. Ibn Kamal Pasha opposed them on both issues. He claimed that Riwayat al-Usul is specific to what is in the six Ummahat, and Zahir al-Riwayah is general, applying to what is outside these six even if it is a rare narration, like the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad on the issue mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira. Similarly, he asserted that a narration from al-Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah without being mentioned in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. And he condemned those who explicitly state the opposite.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of two related issues concerning the hierarchy of transmitted rulings (masail) in the Hanafi school. The author presents and rebuts the position of the prominent Ottoman scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha (d. 940 AH). First, Ibn Kamal Pasha distinguished between 'Riwayat al-Usul' (narrations of the principles) and 'Zahir al-Riwayah' (apparent/authoritative narrations). He claimed that Riwayat al-Usul refers only to the six core books (al-Ummahat al-Sitt) which are the foundations: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat. Meanwhile, he argued that Zahir al-Riwayah is a broader term that can include narrations found in other works, even if they are from the rare transmissions (Nawadir), such as the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad recorded in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira. Second, he claimed that a Nawadir narration can attain the status of Zahir al-Riwayah without ever being mentioned in the six core books. The author, following the vast majority of Hanafi jurists (al-fuqaha), rejects both claims. The established position (taqarrara) is that there is no difference between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah; they are synonymous. Furthermore, a narration from al-Nawadir cannot be considered Zahir al-Riwayah unless it is explicitly mentioned in the books of Usul (i.e., the six core books). Ibn Kamal Pasha's view is thus a minority departure from the consensus. The author notes that Ibn Kamal Pasha criticized those who hold the contrary view, but the criticism is unfounded. This passage is crucial for a mufti to understand that only the rulings in the six books carry the highest authority; rare narrations do not automatically become Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
رواية الأصول (Riwayat al-Usul): Narrations found in the six core books (al-Ummahat al-Sitt) of the Hanafi school.
الأمهات الست (al-Ummahat al-Sitt): The six foundational books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat.
رواية النوادر (Riwayat al-Nawadir): Rare or isolated narrations not included in the six core books, such as those of Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the established Hanafi position (taqarrara), what is the relationship between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) Riwayat al-Usul is a subset of Zahir al-Riwayah.
B) They are synonymous; there is no difference.
C) Zahir al-Riwayah is broader and includes Nawadir.
D) Riwayat al-Usul is only the six books, Zahir al-Riwayah includes all narrations.

Key Takeaway
Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah are synonymous; a narration from al-Nawadir is not considered Zahir al-Riwayah unless mentioned in the books of Usul.

The True Hierarchy of Transmitted Rulings: Zahir al-Riwaya and Riwayat al-Usul Are Identical
Refutes Ibn Kamal Pasha's distinction between Zahir al-Riwaya and Riwayat al-Usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi hierarchy of transmitted rulings by distinguishing between Zahir al-Riwaya and Nawadir, and evaluate Ibn Kamal Pasha's distinction.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwaya = Riwayat al-Usul; a narration is only Zahir al-Riwaya if in the six core books.

A mufti must base his fatwa on the most authoritative narrations. This passage resolves a critical confusion introduced by Ibn Kamal Pasha: whether Zahir al-Riwaya can include rare transmissions (Nawadir) or is strictly limited to the six core books of Imam Muhammad. The commentator affirms the majority position that the two terms are synonymous, ensuring that fatwa rests on the strongest textual foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State Ibn Kamal Pasha's claim that Zahir al-Riwaya is broader than Riwayat al-Usul and can draw from Nawadir, versus the majority view that they are identical and Nawadir alone do not constitute Zahir al-Riwaya.
The dispute is about the definition and scope of the term 'Zahir al-Riwaya'.
2
Analyze the proof
Examine Ibn Kamal's citation of al-Sarakhsi in al-Mabsut, where a narration by Hasan ibn Ziyad is called 'Zahir al-Riwaya' even though it appears in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira (Nawadir). Understand the commentator's refutation: al-Sarakhsi meant that Muhammad also mentioned it in the Usul books.
The key is that the narration must be present in the six books of Usul to be considered Zahir al-Riwaya.
3
Trace the epistemological weight
Understand the authority hierarchy: Zahir al-Riwaya (six books) is the highest layer; Nawadir are supplementary and can coincide with or support Zahir al-Riwaya but do not independently carry the same weight.
The majority holds that Nawadir are not a source for fatwa unless they align with Usul.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a mufti adopts Ibn Kamal's view, he may give weight to a rare transmission not in the six books, potentially issuing a fatwa that contradicts the established school position. The majority view preserves consistency.
The tarjih (preferred position) is that of the majority, as affirmed in the Sharh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد على العلامة ابن كمال باشا في فرقه بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول، وفى زعمه أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية بدون ذكرها في كتب الأصول. هذا وقد فرق العلامة ابن كمال باشا بين رواية الأصول وظاهر الرواية، حيث قال في شرحه على الهداية " في مسألة حج المرأة ما حاصله : إنه ذكر في مبسوط السرخسي ": أن ظاهر الرواية أنه يشترط أن تملك قدر نفقة محرمها ". وإنه ذكر في المحيط و الذخيرة : أنه روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنها إذا قدرت على نفقة نفسها ونفقة محرمها ، لزمها الحج . واضطربت الروايات عن محمد " . ثم قال : " ومن هنا ظهر أن مراد الإمام السرخسي من ظاهر الرواية ، رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة ، واتضح الفرق بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول ؛ إذ المراد من الأصول المبسوط، والجامع الصغير، والجامع الكبير، والزيادات ، والسير الكبير ) ، وليس فيها رواية الحسن، بل كلها رواية رواية الحسن المذكورة في المحيط " و "الذخيرة " التي أطلق عليها السرخسى فى المبسوط كلمة ظاهر الرواية . وأجاب الشارح عن الأول بقوله : "لا يخفى عليك بأن كلام السرخسى لا يدل على ذلك ؛ لأن قوله إنها ظاهر الرواية " ليس معناه : أن رواية الحسن هي ظاهر الرواية لأجل أن الحسن ذكرها ، بل مراده : أن محمداً ذكرها في كتب الأصول أيضا، فهى من الروايات الظاهرة لأجل هذا السبب لا لأن الحسن رواها فحسب، فغاية ما فيه أن رواية النوادر قد توافق ظاهر الرواية، وهذا لا خلاف فيه لأحد ؛ لأنه لا يلزم من ذکر رواية في كتب النوادر أن لا يكون لها ذكر في كتب الأصول أو أن تكون مخالفة لما في كتب الأصول، فكثيراً ما يتفق ما في كتب النوادر بما في كتب ظاهر الروايات وسيأتي الجواب عن الثاني .
Refutation of the scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha regarding his distinction between Zahir al-Riwaya and Riwayat al-Usul, and his claim that Nawadir may be considered Zahir al-Riwaya without being mentioned in the books of Usul. This is while the scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha distinguished between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwaya, as he said in his commentary on al-Hidayah regarding the issue of a woman's Hajj, the summary of which is: 'It is mentioned in Mabsut al-Sarakhsi that the Zahir al-Riwaya is that she must possess the amount for the expenses of her mahram.' And it is mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira that al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that if she can afford her own expenses and that of her mahram, Hajj becomes obligatory upon her. And the narrations from Muhammad are conflicting.' Then he said: 'From this it becomes clear that Imam al-Sarakhsi's meaning of Zahir al-Riwaya was the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, and the difference between Zahir al-Riwaya and Riwayat al-Usul is evident; since what is meant by Usul are al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Siyar al-Kabir, and the narration of al-Hasan is not in them, rather it is all the narration of al-Hasan mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira, which al-Sarakhsi in al-Mabsut referred to as Zahir al-Riwaya.' And the commentator (Sharh) responded to the first (issue) by saying: 'It is not hidden from you that the speech of al-Sarakhsi does not indicate that; because his statement that it is Zahir al-Riwaya does not mean that the narration of al-Hasan is Zahir al-Riwaya merely because al-Hasan narrated it. Rather, his meaning is that Muhammad also mentioned it in the books of Usul, so it is among the apparent narrations for this reason, not simply because al-Hasan narrated it. So the most that can be said is that the Nawadir may agree with Zahir al-Riwaya, and there is no disagreement about this; because the mention of a narration in the books of Nawadir does not necessitate that it is not mentioned in the books of Usul or that it contradicts what is in the books of Usul. Often what is in the books of Nawadir coincides with what is in the books of Zahir al-Riwaya. And the answer to the second (issue) will come later.'
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents a critical refinement of a position taken by the Ottoman scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha (d. 940 AH) regarding the hierarchy of transmitted rulings in the Hanafi school. The issue is twofold: first, whether 'Zahir al-Riwaya' (the dominant/authoritative narrations) is a broader category than 'Riwayat al-Usul' (the six core books of Imam Muhammad), and second, whether a narration from the Nawadir (rare transmissions, e.g., from Hasan ibn Ziyad) can be considered Zahir al-Riwaya even if it is not found in the Usul books. The majority of Hanafi jurists hold that Zahir al-Riwaya is synonymous with Riwayat al-Usul. Ibn Kamal Pasha argued otherwise, citing a passage from al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut where al-Sarakhsi referred to a narration by Hasan ibn Ziyad as 'Zahir al-Riwaya' even though it appears in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira (Nawadir works) and not in the six books. The commentator (Sharh of Rasm al-Mufti) refutes this by explaining that al-Sarakhsi's statement does not prove Ibn Kamal's point; rather, al-Sarakhsi meant that this narration is also mentioned by Muhammad in the Usul books (i.e., it is not exclusively a Nawadir transmission). Thus, the correct understanding is that Nawadir may coincide with Zahir al-Riwaya, but they are not considered Zahir al-Riwaya unless they are also found in the six books. The second issue (whether Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwaya without being in Usul) is deferred to a later discussion.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwaya): The dominant and authoritative narrations within the Hanafi school, transmitted via reliable chains. According to this passage, it is synonymous with Riwayat al-Usul.
رواية الأصول (Riwayat al-Usul): Narrations contained in the foundational (usul) books, i.e., the six books of Imam Muhammad. The commentator equates this with Zahir al-Riwaya.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare transmissions, particularly those not found in the six books of Usul, such as narrations of Hasan ibn Ziyad. They are less authoritative than Zahir al-Riwaya but may be considered if they agree with Usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator in this passage, what is the correct understanding of al-Sarakhsi's use of 'Zahir al-Riwaya' for the narration of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad?
A) He meant it is Zahir al-Riwaya solely because al-Hasan narrated it.
B) He meant it is Zahir al-Riwaya because Muhammad also mentioned it in the Usul books.
C) He meant it is Zahir al-Riwaya because it appears in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira.
D) He mistakenly called it Zahir al-Riwaya; it should be considered Nawadir.

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwaya and Riwayat al-Usul are identical; a narration is only considered Zahir al-Riwaya if it is found in the six books of Imam Muhammad, regardless of its presence in Nawadir works.

Defining Zahir al-Riwayah vs Riwayat al-Usul
Refuting Ibn Kamal Pasha's distinction between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the majority view (Jumhur) from Ibn Kamal Pasha's view on the relationship between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul, and apply the correct definition to classify a given narration as Zahir al-Riwayah or not.

Core Idea
For the majority, Zahir al-Riwayah = Riwayat al-Usul; a narration must be in the six books to be fatwa-authoritative.

This passage addresses a key debate in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the precise definition of 'Zahir al-Riwayah' (apparent transmissions) versus 'Riwayat al-Usul' (transmissions of the foundational books). Ibn Kamal Pasha argued that Zahir al-Riwayah is broader and could include narrations from the Nawadir (rare books), but the majority of Hanafi scholars reject this. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a mufti to correctly weigh evidence and issue fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing definitions
Extract the definitions presented: (a) Majority view: Zahir al-Riwayah = Riwayat al-Usul, restricted to the six foundational books of Imam Muhammad. (b) Ibn Kamal Pasha's view: Riwayat al-Usul is specific, Zahir al-Riwayah is general and may include narrations from outside the six books.
Note that the six books are: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Saghir (according to most).
2
Examine the evidence used by each side
Ibn Kamal Pasha cites a case from al-Mabsut where al-Sarakhsi calls a narration by Hasan ibn Ziyad 'Zahir al-Riwayah', and argues that this narration is only found in the Nawadir, not the Usul. The author counters that al-Sarakhsi's statement implies that Muhammad also transmitted it in the foundational books.
Observe how Ibn Kamal Pasha uses al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira as sources for the narration.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Ibn Kamal Pasha's inference
The author argues that the presence of a narration in the Nawadir does not preclude its presence in the Usul. In the specific case, the narration is also in the Usul, so al-Sarakhsi's labeling is consistent with the majority view. The author emphasizes that the Nawadir may coincide with Zahir al-Riwayah, but that does not make them equivalent.
Key phrase: 'فغاية ما فيه أن رواية النوادر قد توافق ظاهر الرواية' – the utmost is that a Nawadir narration may agree with Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
State the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence: if Ibn Kamal Pasha's view were accepted, rulings from Nawadir alone could gain the same authority as Zahir al-Riwayah, weakening the evidentiary hierarchy. The mufta bihi position is the majority view: a narration is Zahir al-Riwayah only if it is in the six foundational books.
The author defends the commentators of al-Hidayah who were criticized by Ibn Kamal Pasha, asserting they correctly equate the two categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الردّ علی ابن باشاه في مسألتين الرواية، حيث قال في شرحه على الهداية " في مسألة حج المرأة ما حاصله : إنه ذكر في مبسوط السرخسي " : أن ظاهر الرواية أنه يشترط أن تملك قدر نفقة محرمها " . وإنه ذكر في المحيط و الذخيرة : أنه روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنها إذا قدرت على نفقة نفسها ونفقة محرمها ، لزمها الحج . واضطربت الروايات عن محمد " .
ثم قال : " ومن هنا ظهر أن مراد الإمام السرخسي من ظاهر الرواية ، رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة ، واتضح الفرق بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول ؛ إذ المراد من الأصول المبسوط، والجامع الصغير، والجامع الكبير، والزيادات ، والسير الكبير ) ، وليس فيها رواية الحسن، بل كلها رواية
(۲)
ومستدلّه في المسألتين رواية الحسن المذكورة في المحيط " و "الذخيرة " التي أطلق عليها السرخسى فى المبسوط كلمة ظاهر الرواية . وأجاب الشارح عن الأول بقوله : "لا يخفى عليك بأن كلام السرخسى لا يدل على ذلك ؛ لأن قوله إنها ظاهر الرواية " ليس معناه : أن رواية الحسن هي ظاهر الرواية لأجل أن الحسن ذكرها ، بل مراده : أن محمداً ذكرها في كتب الأصول أيضا، فهى من الروايات الظاهرة لأجل هذا السبب لا لأن الحسن رواها فحسب، فغاية ما فيه أن رواية النوادر قد توافق ظاهر الرواية، وهذا لا خلاف فيه لأحد ؛ لأنه لا يلزم من ذکر رواية في كتب النوادر أن لا يكون لها ذكر في كتب الأصول أو أن تكون مخالفة لما في كتب الأصول، فكثيراً ما يتفق ما في كتب النوادر بما في كتب ظاهر الروايات وسيأتي الجواب عن الثاني .
(۱) قوله : " واتضح الفرق " بيان للاختلاف الأول، فعند الجمهور ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول متساويان، وعند العلامة رواية الأصول خاص وظاهر الرواية عام فرواية الأصول ما روى عن محمد في كتبه الستة، وظاهر الرواية قد تكون فيها - وهو أكثر وقد تكون في غيرها كرواية الحسن في هذه المسألة .
وقوله : "وعلم . . . " هذا اختلاف ثان، فعند الجمهور كون رواية النوادر من الروايات الظاهرة مشروط بذكرها في كتب الأصول وعند العلامة غير مشروط به . (۲) قوله : "والسير الكبير " لم يذكر هنا السير الصغير ؛ إما لأنه سقط سهواً، وإما لأن

٧٤
شرح عقود رسم المفتی الردّ علی ابن باشاه في مسألتين محمد وعلم أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية، والمراد من رواية النوادر رواية غير الأصول المذكورة. فاحفظ هذا ! فإن شراح هذا الكتاب قد غفلوا عنه، وقد صرح بعضهم بعدم الفرق بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول، وزعم أن رواية النوادر لا تكون ظاهر الرواية " . أقول : لا يخفى عليك أن قول "المحيط" و "الذخيرة" : "إن هذه رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة"، لا يلزم منه أن تكون مخالفة لرواية الأصول، فقد يكون رواها الحسن في كتب النوادر ، ورواها محمد في كتب الأصول، وإنما ذكر رواية الحسن لعدم الاضطراب عنه، بدليل قوله : واضطربت الروايات عن محمد ، وحينئذ، فقول السرخسي : "إنها ظاهر الرواية " . معناه : أن محمداً ذكرها في كتب الأصول، فهي إحدى الروايات عنه، وحينئذ (۱) فلم يلزم منه أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية نعم تكون ظاهر الرواية إذا ذكرت فى كتب الأصول أيضا كهذه المسألة ؛ فإن ذكرها في كتب النوادر لا يلزم منه أن لا يكون لها ذكر في كتب الأصول، وإنما يصح ما قاله أن لو ثبت أن هذه المسألة لا ذكر لها في كتب ظاهر الرواية، وعبارة "المحيط " و "الذخيرة لا تدل على ذلك، وحينئذ فلا وجه الجزمه
بالغفلة على شراح "الهداية " الموافق كلامهم لما قدمناه، والله تعالى أعلم .
المعتاد ذكر السير بقسميه معا فذكر أحدهما يغنى عن ذكر الآخر، وذكر العلامة اللكنوي في "عمدة الرعاية " أن بعضهم لم يعد السير الصغير من الأصول، فيمكن أن يكون ابن كمال باشا اختار هذا القول .
(۱) قوله : "وحينئذ ردّ على قوله الثاني، أى إذا لم يلزم من رواية الحسن مسألة أن لا تكون مذكورة في كتب ظاهر الرواية، لم يلزم أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية بدون الذكر في الكتب الستة، بل تكون ظاهر الرواية إذا ذكرت في تلك الكتب أيضا ؛ فإنه إذا وافق نادر الرواية بما في كتب الأصول يعد من ظاهر الرواية، فاستدلال العلامة لا يتم إلا إذا استشهد بمسألة أطلق عليها ظاهر الرواية من غير أن يكون لها ذكر في كتب ظاهر الرواية، لا لفظا ولا معنى
The refutation of Ibn Kamal Pasha in two issues of transmission: He said in his commentary on al-Hidayah concerning the issue of a woman's Hajj, the summary of which: It is mentioned in al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi: 'That apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) requires that she possess the amount of expenditure for her mahram.' And it is mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira: That al-Hasan related from Abu Hanifa that if she can afford her own expenditure and that of her mahram, Hajj becomes obligatory upon her. And the transmissions from Muhammad were conflicting.' Then he said: 'And from here it becomes clear that the intention of Imam al-Sarakhsi from 'Zahir al-Riwayah' is the transmission of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, and the difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul becomes apparent; because what is meant by al-Usul are al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Siyar al-Kabir), and in them is not the transmission of al-Hasan, rather all are transmissions (of Muhammad). (2) And his evidence in the two issues is the transmission of al-Hasan mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira, to which al-Sarakhsi applied the term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' in al-Mabsut. And the commentator answered the first (point) by saying: 'It is not hidden from you that the statement of al-Sarakhsi does not indicate that; because his saying that it is 'Zahir al-Riwayah' does not mean that al-Hasan's transmission is Zahir al-Riwayah because al-Hasan transmitted it, rather his intention is that Muhammad also mentioned it in the foundational books, so it is among the apparent transmissions for this reason, not because al-Hasan simply transmitted it. The utmost of it is that a narration from the Nawadir may coincide with Zahir al-Riwayah, and there is no disagreement about this from anyone; because the mere mention of a narration in the Nawadir books does not necessitate that it has no mention in the foundational books or that it contradicts what is in the foundational books. Many times what is in the Nawadir books agrees with what is in the books of apparent transmissions. And the answer to the second (point) will come later.' (1) His statement: 'and the difference becomes clear' is an explanation of the first disagreement. For according to the majority, Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul are equivalent, while according to the scholar (Ibn Kamal Pasha), Riwayat al-Usul is specific and Zahir al-Riwayah is general. Thus Riwayat al-Usul is what was transmitted from Muhammad in his six books, while Zahir al-Riwayah may be in them—which is most cases—and may be outside them like al-Hasan's transmission in this issue. And his statement: 'and it became known...' is a second disagreement. According to the majority, a narration from the Nawadir being among the apparent transmissions is conditional upon its mention in the foundational books, while according to the scholar (Ibn Kamal Pasha) it is not conditional. (2) His statement: 'and al-Siyar al-Kabir' — here he did not mention al-Siyar al-Saghir, either because it was omitted inadvertently, or because... It is customary to mention the two Siyars together, so mentioning one suffices from mentioning the other. And al-Allamah al-Lakhnawi mentioned in 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah that some did not count al-Siyar al-Saghir among the foundational books, so it is possible that Ibn Kamal Pasha chose this opinion. Page 74: ...and it became known that a narration from the Nawadir may be Zahir al-Riwayah, and what is meant by Nawadir is narration other than the aforementioned foundational books. So memorize this! For the commentators of this book have neglected it, and some of them have explicitly stated that there is no difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul, and claimed that a narration from the Nawadir is not Zahir al-Riwayah. I say: It is not hidden from you that the statement of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira: 'This is the transmission of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa' does not necessitate that it contradicts the transmission of the foundational books. It is possible that al-Hasan transmitted it in the Nawadir books, and Muhammad transmitted it in the foundational books. They only mentioned al-Hasan's transmission because of the lack of conflict from him, evidenced by his statement: 'and the transmissions from Muhammad were conflicting.' At that point, al-Sarakhsi's statement: 'It is Zahir al-Riwayah' means that Muhammad mentioned it in the foundational books, so it is one of the transmissions from him. At that point, (1) it does not follow from this that a narration from the Nawadir may be Zahir al-Riwayah. Yes, it is Zahir al-Riwayah if it is also mentioned in the foundational books, like this issue. For its mention in the Nawadir books does not necessitate that it has no mention in the foundational books. His statement would only be correct if it were established that this issue has no mention in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. And the wording of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira does not indicate that. At that point, there is no basis for him to assert negligence upon the commentators of al-Hidayah, whose statement agrees with what we have presented. And Allah knows best. (1) His statement: 'At that point' is a refutation of his second statement, meaning: If it does not follow from the issue of al-Hasan's transmission that it is not mentioned in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, then it does not follow that a narration from the Nawadir may be Zahir al-Riwayah without mention in the six books. Rather, it is Zahir al-Riwayah if it is mentioned in those books as well. For if a rare narration agrees with what is in the foundational books, it is counted as Zahir al-Riwayah. Thus the scholar's (Ibn Kamal Pasha's) inference is incomplete unless he provides evidence of an issue called 'Zahir al-Riwayah' without being mentioned in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, neither in wording nor meaning.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary by the author (likely Allamah al-Lakhnawi) refuting Ibn Kamal Pasha's views on the definitions and relationship between 'Zahir al-Riwayah' and 'Riwayat al-Usul'. The author argues that according to the majority of Hanafi scholars, Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul are equivalent, meaning the six foundational books of Imam Muhammad (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Saghir according to some). Ibn Kamal Pasha, however, distinguishes between them: he considers Riwayat al-Usul as only the narrations found in those six books, while Zahir al-Riwayah is broader and can include narrations from other sources, like the transmission of Hasan ibn Ziyad. The author refutes this by analyzing a specific example: the issue of a woman's Hajj where al-Sarakhsi called a narration transmitted by Hasan 'Zahir al-Riwayah'. Ibn Kamal Pasha claimed this shows that a narration from the Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah without being in the Usul. The author explains that al-Sarakhsi's statement actually implies that Muhammad also transmitted that narration in his foundational books, making it part of Riwayat al-Usul. The author emphasizes that mentioning 'al-Hasan's transmission' in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira does not negate its presence in the Usul; it is simply to clarify the source due to conflicting reports from Muhammad. The passage concludes that a narration is considered Zahir al-Riwayah only if it is found in the six foundational books, whether it also appears in the Nawadir or not. The author defends the commentators of al-Hidayah who have been criticized by Ibn Kamal Pasha, asserting that they are correct in equating the two categories.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): Apparent transmissions: narrations that are widely transmitted and recorded in the six foundational books of Imam Muhammad, forming the primary authority for fatwa.
رواية الأصول (Riwayat al-Usul): Transmissions of the foundational books: the narrations recorded by Imam Muhammad in his six major works.
رواية النوادر (Riwayat al-Nawadir): Rare transmissions: narrations found in works other than the six foundational books, such as those of Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of this passage, what is the relationship between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul?
A) They are entirely distinct categories with no overlap.
B) Riwayat al-Usul is a subset of the broader Zahir al-Riwayah.
C) They are equivalent; both refer to narrations in the six foundational books.
D) Zahir al-Riwayah is a subset of Riwayat al-Usul.

Key Takeaway
A narration is Zahir al-Riwayah only if it is recorded in the six foundational books of Imam Muhammad; the majority equates this with Riwayat al-Usul, and Ibn Kamal Pasha's broader definition is rejected.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
12 min
When Can Nawadir Be Zahir al-Riwayah?
Refuting Ibn Kamal Pasha on Nawadir and Zahir al-Riwayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the criterion that a Nawadir narration becomes Zahir al-Riwayah if also recorded in the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A narration from Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah if it appears in the six core books.

Some Hanafi scholars assert that narrations from al-Nawadir (rare transmissions) can never be considered Zahir al-Riwayah. In this passage, the Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti refutes that claim by analyzing the statements of early authorities. You will learn the precise condition under which a rare narration rises to the highest level of authority and why Ibn Kamal Pasha's position is incorrect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the two opposing views: Ibn Kamal Pasha's categorical denial vs. the author's conditional acceptance.
Note that the author aligns with al-Sarakhsi and al-Lakhnawi.
2
Analyze the evidence from al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira
These works cite a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. The author argues this does not prove absence from al-usul.
The citation may be due to its consistency, not exclusivity.
3
Understand al-Sarakhsi's reasoning
Al-Sarakhsi calls it Zahir al-Riwayah because Muhammad mentioned it in the books of principles.
This shows that being in Nawadir does not preclude being in al-usul.
4
Apply the condition
A Nawadir narration becomes Zahir al-Riwayah if it is also found in the six core books, either in wording or meaning.
The burden of proof is on the claimant of absence.
5
Determine the fatwa hierarchy
Identify that such a narration carries the authority of Zahir al-Riwayah and thus takes precedence in fatwa.
This affects which ruling is mufta bihi.

الردّ على ابن باشاه في مسألتين محمد وعلم أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية، والمراد من رواية النوادر رواية غير الأصول المذكورة. فاحفظ هذا ! فإن شراح هذا الكتاب قد غفلوا عنه، وقد صرح بعضهم بعدم الفرق بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول، وزعم أن رواية النوادر لا تكون ظاهر الرواية . أقول : لا يخفى عليك أن قول "المحيط" و "الذخيرة" : "إن هذه رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة"، لا يلزم منه أن تكون مخالفة لرواية الأصول، فقد يكون رواها الحسن في كتب النوادر ، ورواها محمد في كتب الأصول، وإنما ذكر رواية الحسن لعدم الاضطراب عنه، بدليل قوله : واضطربت الروايات عن محمد ، وحينئذ، فقول السرخسي : "إنها ظاهر الرواية" . معناه : أن محمداً ذكرها في كتب الأصول، فهي إحدى الروايات عنه، وحينئذ فلم يلزم منه أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية نعم تكون ظاهر الرواية إذا ذكرت فى كتب الأصول أيضا كهذه المسألة ؛ فإن ذكرها في كتب النوادر لا يلزم منه أن لا يكون لها ذكر في كتب الأصول، وإنما يصح ما قاله أن لو ثبت أن هذه المسألة لا ذكر لها في كتب ظاهر الرواية، وعبارة "المحيط " و "الذخيرة لا تدل على ذلك، وحينئذ فلا وجه الجزمه بالغفلة على شراح "الهداية " الموافق كلامهم لما قدمناه، والله تعالى أعلم . المعتاد ذكر السير بقسميه معا فذكر أحدهما يغنى عن ذكر الآخر، وذكر العلامة اللكنوي في "عمدة الرعاية " أن بعضهم لم يعد السير الصغير من الأصول، فيمكن أن يكون ابن كمال باشا اختار هذا القول . (۱) قوله : "وحينئذ ردّ على قوله الثاني، أى إذا لم يلزم من رواية الحسن مسألة أن لا تكون مذكورة في كتب ظاهر الرواية، لم يلزم أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية بدون الذكر في الكتب الستة، بل تكون ظاهر الرواية إذا ذكرت في تلك الكتب أيضا ؛ فإنه إذا وافق نادر الرواية بما في كتب الأصول يعد من ظاهر الرواية، فاستدلال العلامة لا يتم إلا إذا استشهد بمسألة أطلق عليها ظاهر الرواية من غير أن يكون لها ذكر في كتب ظاهر الرواية، لا لفظا ولا معنى مطلب في تحقيق لفظ السير تتمة : السير جمع سيرة وهي الطريقة في الأمور. وفي الشرع : تختص بسير النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم في مغازيه، كذا في "الهداية " . قال في "المغرب" : "وقالوا : السير الكبير، فوصفوها بصفة المذكر ؛ لقيامها مقام المضاف الذى هو كتاب كقولهم : صلاة الظهر ) . وسير الكبير خطأ كجامع الصغير، وجامع الكبير " . اهـ . وحينئذ فالسير الكبير بكسر السين وفتح الياء على لفظ الجمع لا بفتح السين وسكون الياء على لفظ المفرد، كما ينطق به بعض من لا معرفة له . -۱۷ - وَاشْتَهرَ المَبْسُوط بالأصل وَذَا لسبقه السِّيِّةَ تَصْنَيْفًا كَذَا ١٨- الجَامِعُ الصَّغِيرُ بَعْدَهُ فَمَا فِيهِ عَلَى الأَصْلِ لِذَا تَقَدَمًا ١٩ - وآخِرُ السَّنَةِ تَصْنِيفًا وَرَدْ السَّيِّرُ الكَبِيرُ فَهُوَ المُعْتَمَد (۱) قوله : صلاة الظهر" به ظهر أن ما في نسخة "المغرب" التي عندى من قوله : صلى الظهر " بدل "صلاة الظهر - تحريف من النساخ ، فليس بصحيح . (مظ) (۲) قوله : "وذا" أى كونه أصلا، وقوله : "لذا " أى لأجل أن الجامع الصغير صنف بعد الأصل وصار بمنزلة الناسخ له يتقدّم عليه عند التعارض .
The refutation of Ibn Kamal Pasha regarding two issues: Muhammad (al-Shaybani) knew that the narration of al-Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah, and the meaning of 'narration of al-Nawadir' is narration other than the mentioned principles (al-usul). Memorize this! For the commentators of this book have been heedless of it, and some have explicitly claimed no difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and the narration of the principles, and claimed that the narration of al-Nawadir cannot be Zahir al-Riwayah. I say: It is not hidden from you that the statement of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira: 'This is the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa' does not necessarily entail that it contradicts the narration of the principles. It is possible that al-Hasan narrated it in the books of Nawadir, and Muhammad narrated it in the books of principles. He only mentioned al-Hasan's narration because there is no inconsistency from him, as evidenced by his statement: 'And the narrations from Muhammad are inconsistent.' In that case, al-Sarakhsi's statement: 'It is Zahir al-Riwayah' means that Muhammad mentioned it in the books of principles, so it is one of the narrations from him. So then it does not necessarily follow that the narration of al-Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah. Yes, it becomes Zahir al-Riwayah if it is also mentioned in the books of principles, like this issue; for its mention in the books of Nawadir does not necessitate that it has no mention in the books of principles. His statement would be valid only if it were established that this issue has no mention in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. The wording of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira does not indicate that. So there is no justification for his assertion of heedlessness against the commentators of al-Hidayah, whose words agree with what we have presented. And Allah knows best. It is customary to mention al-Siyar with both parts together, so mentioning one suffices for the other. And Allamah al-Lakhnawi mentioned in 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah that some did not count al-Siyar al-Saghir among the principles, so it is possible that Ibn Kamal Pasha chose this view. (1) His statement: 'Then there is a refutation of his second statement,' meaning when it is not necessary from al-Hasan's narration of an issue that it is not mentioned in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, it does not follow that narration of al-Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah without mention in the six books; rather it is Zahir al-Riwayah if also mentioned in those books. For if a rare narration agrees with what is in the books of principles, it is counted as Zahir al-Riwayah. So the proof of the scholar is not complete unless he cites an issue that is called Zahir al-Riwayah without having mention in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, neither in wording nor meaning. Section on verifying the word al-Siyar: Supplementary: al-Siyar is the plural of sirah, meaning a method in matters. And in the Sacred Law, it is specific to the Sirah (biography) of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in his military expeditions. Thus it is in al-Hidayah. He said in al-Mughrib: 'They said: al-Siyar al-Kabir, so they described it with the masculine attribute because it stands in place of the omitted noun which is 'kitab' (book), like their saying: 'Salat al-Zuhr' (Zuhr prayer). And 'Sayr al-Kabir' is a mistake, like 'Jami' al-Saghir' and 'Jami' al-Kabir.' End quote. So then al-Siyar al-Kabir is with kasra on the sin and fatha on the ya, in the plural form, not with fatha on the sin and sukun on the ya in the singular form, as some without knowledge pronounce it. 17- Al-Mabsut is famous as the original (asl), and that is because it preceded the six works in composition. 18- Al-Jami' al-Saghir came after it, so whatever is in it is according to the original, so it takes precedence. 19- And at the end of the year in composition came al-Siyar al-Kabir, so it is the relied-upon (mu'tamad). (1) His statement: 'Salat al-Zuhr' shows that what is in the copy of al-Mughrib that I have, from his statement: 'Salla al-Zuhr' instead of 'Salat al-Zuhr', is a corruption by copyists, so it is not correct. (Mazhar) (2) His statement: 'wa dha' means its being the original (asl), and his statement: 'li dha' means because al-Jami' al-Saghir was composed after the original and became like an abrogator (nasikh) of it, so it takes precedence in cases of conflict.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on the classification of Hanafi legal works. The author refutes Ibn Kamal Pasha's claim that narrations from al-Nawadir (rare transmissions) cannot be considered Zahir al-Riwayah. The author argues that a narration can be Zahir al-Riwayah if it is also recorded in the six core books (al-usul) of Imam Muhammad, even if it is also found in al-Nawadir. He explains that the statement in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira calling a narration from al-Hasan does not necessarily imply it is not in the principles; it may simply be that al-Hasan's version is cited because it is more consistent, while Muhammad's version is found elsewhere. The author emphasizes that the commentators of al-Hidayah were not heedless, as Ibn Kamal Pasha claimed. The passage then defines the term 'al-Siyar' (plural of sirah) in the legal context, specifically referring to the Prophet's military expeditions. It corrects a common mispronunciation: al-Siyar al-Kabir should be read with a kasra on the sin (al-Siyar) as a plural, not as 'Sayr' singular. The poetic lines at the end confirm the order of composition: al-Mabsut is the original, al-Jami' al-Saghir comes after it and supersedes it, and al-Siyar al-Kabir is the latest and is the mu'tamad (relied-upon opinion). This illustrates the hierarchy of Hanafi texts and how later works (al-Jami' al-Saghir) can abrogate earlier ones (al-Mabsut) in case of conflict.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat. Rulings from these carry the highest authority in the Hanafi school.
رواية النوادر (Riwayat al-Nawadir): Rare or uncommon transmissions, such as those transmitted by Hasan ibn Ziyad or other students, which are not part of the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, a narration from al-Nawadir can be considered Zahir al-Riwayah if:
A) It is transmitted by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.
B) It is also mentioned in one of the six core books.
C) It is preferred by the majority of later scholars.
D) It is found in al-Mabsut only.

Key Takeaway
A Nawadir narration becomes Zahir al-Riwayah if corroborated in the six core books; otherwise, it remains of lower authority.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Defining 'al-Siyar' and the Hierarchy of Hanafi Works
Defining al-Siyar and listing the order of Hanafi works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of al-Siyar in Hanafi legal terminology and recite the correct pronunciation and order of the six core works.

Core Idea
Al-Siyar refers to the Prophet's military expeditions; al-Siyar al-Kabir is the last composed and the mu'tamad.

The passage now turns to clarifying the term 'al-Siyar' used in the titles of two seminal Hanafi works. You will learn why it is plural, how it is correctly pronounced, and how the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah are ranked in terms of composition and authority. This knowledge is essential for properly citing Hanafi sources in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic definition
Al-Siyar (السير) is the plural of sirah (سيرة), meaning a method or way. In the Sacred Law, it specifically refers to the Prophet's biography in his military expeditions (maghazi).
This usage is fixed in Hanafi terminology.
2
Correct the pronunciation
The correct pronunciation is 'al-Siyar al-Kabir' with kasra on the sin and fatha on the ya, as a plural. Incorrectly pronouncing it as 'Sayr' (singular) is a common mistake.
Al-Mughrib uses the example of 'Salat al-Zuhr' to illustrate the grammatical construction.
3
Identify the two works
There are two works: al-Siyar al-Saghir and al-Siyar al-Kabir, both by Imam Muhammad. They are often mentioned together.
Some scholars did not count al-Siyar al-Saghir among the principles, but the author considers the pair as part of the six.
4
Memorize the order of composition
Based on the poetic lines: al-Mabsut is the original (asl) and first composed. Then al-Jami' al-Saghir, which takes precedence over al-Mabsut when they conflict. Finally al-Siyar al-Kabir, the last composed, is the mu'tamad.
The order matters for resolving contradictions: later works may abrogate earlier ones.
5
Apply in fatwa
When citing works, one must know which is the mu'tamad. For siyar matters, al-Siyar al-Kabir is the relied-upon source.
This affects which ruling is given priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الردّ على ابن باشاه في مسألتين محمد وعلم أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية، والمراد من رواية النوادر رواية غير الأصول المذكورة. فاحفظ هذا ! فإن شراح هذا الكتاب قد غفلوا عنه، وقد صرح بعضهم بعدم الفرق بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول، وزعم أن رواية النوادر لا تكون ظاهر الرواية . أقول : لا يخفى عليك أن قول "المحيط" و "الذخيرة" : "إن هذه رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة"، لا يلزم منه أن تكون مخالفة لرواية الأصول، فقد يكون رواها الحسن في كتب النوادر ، ورواها محمد في كتب الأصول، وإنما ذكر رواية الحسن لعدم الاضطراب عنه، بدليل قوله : واضطربت الروايات عن محمد ، وحينئذ، فقول السرخسي : "إنها ظاهر الرواية" . معناه : أن محمداً ذكرها في كتب الأصول، فهي إحدى الروايات عنه، وحينئذ فلم يلزم منه أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية نعم تكون ظاهر الرواية إذا ذكرت فى كتب الأصول أيضا كهذه المسألة ؛ فإن ذكرها في كتب النوادر لا يلزم منه أن لا يكون لها ذكر في كتب الأصول، وإنما يصح ما قاله أن لو ثبت أن هذه المسألة لا ذكر لها في كتب ظاهر الرواية، وعبارة "المحيط " و "الذخيرة لا تدل على ذلك، وحينئذ فلا وجه الجزمه بالغفلة على شراح "الهداية " الموافق كلامهم لما قدمناه، والله تعالى أعلم . المعتاد ذكر السير بقسميه معا فذكر أحدهما يغنى عن ذكر الآخر، وذكر العلامة اللكنوي في "عمدة الرعاية " أن بعضهم لم يعد السير الصغير من الأصول، فيمكن أن يكون ابن كمال باشا اختار هذا القول . (۱) قوله : "وحينئذ ردّ على قوله الثاني، أى إذا لم يلزم من رواية الحسن مسألة أن لا تكون مذكورة في كتب ظاهر الرواية، لم يلزم أن رواية النوادر قد تكون ظاهر الرواية بدون الذكر في الكتب الستة، بل تكون ظاهر الرواية إذا ذكرت في تلك الكتب أيضا ؛ فإنه إذا وافق نادر الرواية بما في كتب الأصول يعد من ظاهر الرواية، فاستدلال العلامة لا يتم إلا إذا استشهد بمسألة أطلق عليها ظاهر الرواية من غير أن يكون لها ذكر في كتب ظاهر الرواية، لا لفظا ولا معنى مطلب في تحقيق لفظ السير تتمة : السير جمع سيرة وهي الطريقة في الأمور. وفي الشرع : تختص بسير النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم في مغازيه، كذا في "الهداية " . قال في "المغرب" : "وقالوا : السير الكبير، فوصفوها بصفة المذكر ؛ لقيامها مقام المضاف الذى هو كتاب كقولهم : صلاة الظهر ) . وسير الكبير خطأ كجامع الصغير، وجامع الكبير " . اهـ . وحينئذ فالسير الكبير بكسر السين وفتح الياء على لفظ الجمع لا بفتح السين وسكون الياء على لفظ المفرد، كما ينطق به بعض من لا معرفة له . -۱۷ - وَاشْتَهرَ المَبْسُوط بالأصل وَذَا لسبقه السِّيِّةَ تَصْنَيْفًا كَذَا ١٨- الجَامِعُ الصَّغِيرُ بَعْدَهُ فَمَا فِيهِ عَلَى الأَصْلِ لِذَا تَقَدَمًا ١٩ - وآخِرُ السَّنَةِ تَصْنِيفًا وَرَدْ السَّيِّرُ الكَبِيرُ فَهُوَ المُعْتَمَد (۱) قوله : صلاة الظهر" به ظهر أن ما في نسخة "المغرب" التي عندى من قوله : صلى الظهر " بدل "صلاة الظهر - تحريف من النساخ ، فليس بصحيح . (مظ) (۲) قوله : "وذا" أى كونه أصلا، وقوله : "لذا " أى لأجل أن الجامع الصغير صنف بعد الأصل وصار بمنزلة الناسخ له يتقدّم عليه عند التعارض .
The refutation of Ibn Kamal Pasha regarding two issues: Muhammad (al-Shaybani) knew that the narration of al-Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah, and the meaning of 'narration of al-Nawadir' is narration other than the mentioned principles (al-usul). Memorize this! For the commentators of this book have been heedless of it, and some have explicitly claimed no difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and the narration of the principles, and claimed that the narration of al-Nawadir cannot be Zahir al-Riwayah. I say: It is not hidden from you that the statement of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira: 'This is the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa' does not necessarily entail that it contradicts the narration of the principles. It is possible that al-Hasan narrated it in the books of Nawadir, and Muhammad narrated it in the books of principles. He only mentioned al-Hasan's narration because there is no inconsistency from him, as evidenced by his statement: 'And the narrations from Muhammad are inconsistent.' In that case, al-Sarakhsi's statement: 'It is Zahir al-Riwayah' means that Muhammad mentioned it in the books of principles, so it is one of the narrations from him. So then it does not necessarily follow that the narration of al-Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah. Yes, it becomes Zahir al-Riwayah if it is also mentioned in the books of principles, like this issue; for its mention in the books of Nawadir does not necessitate that it has no mention in the books of principles. His statement would be valid only if it were established that this issue has no mention in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. The wording of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira does not indicate that. So there is no justification for his assertion of heedlessness against the commentators of al-Hidayah, whose words agree with what we have presented. And Allah knows best. It is customary to mention al-Siyar with both parts together, so mentioning one suffices for the other. And Allamah al-Lakhnawi mentioned in 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah that some did not count al-Siyar al-Saghir among the principles, so it is possible that Ibn Kamal Pasha chose this view. (1) His statement: 'Then there is a refutation of his second statement,' meaning when it is not necessary from al-Hasan's narration of an issue that it is not mentioned in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, it does not follow that narration of al-Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah without mention in the six books; rather it is Zahir al-Riwayah if also mentioned in those books. For if a rare narration agrees with what is in the books of principles, it is counted as Zahir al-Riwayah. So the proof of the scholar is not complete unless he cites an issue that is called Zahir al-Riwayah without having mention in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, neither in wording nor meaning. Section on verifying the word al-Siyar: Supplementary: al-Siyar is the plural of sirah, meaning a method in matters. And in the Sacred Law, it is specific to the Sirah (biography) of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in his military expeditions. Thus it is in al-Hidayah. He said in al-Mughrib: 'They said: al-Siyar al-Kabir, so they described it with the masculine attribute because it stands in place of the omitted noun which is 'kitab' (book), like their saying: 'Salat al-Zuhr' (Zuhr prayer). And 'Sayr al-Kabir' is a mistake, like 'Jami' al-Saghir' and 'Jami' al-Kabir.' End quote. So then al-Siyar al-Kabir is with kasra on the sin and fatha on the ya, in the plural form, not with fatha on the sin and sukun on the ya in the singular form, as some without knowledge pronounce it. 17- Al-Mabsut is famous as the original (asl), and that is because it preceded the six works in composition. 18- Al-Jami' al-Saghir came after it, so whatever is in it is according to the original, so it takes precedence. 19- And at the end of the year in composition came al-Siyar al-Kabir, so it is the relied-upon (mu'tamad). (1) His statement: 'Salat al-Zuhr' shows that what is in the copy of al-Mughrib that I have, from his statement: 'Salla al-Zuhr' instead of 'Salat al-Zuhr', is a corruption by copyists, so it is not correct. (Mazhar) (2) His statement: 'wa dha' means its being the original (asl), and his statement: 'li dha' means because al-Jami' al-Saghir was composed after the original and became like an abrogator (nasikh) of it, so it takes precedence in cases of conflict.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on the classification of Hanafi legal works. The author refutes Ibn Kamal Pasha's claim that narrations from al-Nawadir (rare transmissions) cannot be considered Zahir al-Riwayah. The author argues that a narration can be Zahir al-Riwayah if it is also recorded in the six core books (al-usul) of Imam Muhammad, even if it is also found in al-Nawadir. He explains that the statement in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira calling a narration from al-Hasan does not necessarily imply it is not in the principles; it may simply be that al-Hasan's version is cited because it is more consistent, while Muhammad's version is found elsewhere. The author emphasizes that the commentators of al-Hidayah were not heedless, as Ibn Kamal Pasha claimed. The passage then defines the term 'al-Siyar' (plural of sirah) in the legal context, specifically referring to the Prophet's military expeditions. It corrects a common mispronunciation: al-Siyar al-Kabir should be read with a kasra on the sin (al-Siyar) as a plural, not as 'Sayr' singular. The poetic lines at the end confirm the order of composition: al-Mabsut is the original, al-Jami' al-Saghir comes after it and supersedes it, and al-Siyar al-Kabir is the latest and is the mu'tamad (relied-upon opinion). This illustrates the hierarchy of Hanafi texts and how later works (al-Jami' al-Saghir) can abrogate earlier ones (al-Mabsut) in case of conflict.

Key Terms
السير الكبير (al-Siyar al-Kabir): One of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, composed by Imam Muhammad, dealing with the Prophet's military expeditions and rules of jihad. It is the last in composition and is the mu'tamad (relied-upon work) in its field.
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): The first and most voluminous of the six core books, composed by Imam Muhammad. It is considered the original (asl) in terms of composition.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): One of the six core books, composed after al-Mabsut. It is considered to have a superseding authority over al-Mabsut when they disagree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the poetic verses in this passage, which work is the mu'tamad (relied-upon) in the field of siyar?
A) al-Mabsut
B) al-Jami' al-Saghir
C) al-Siyar al-Kabir
D) al-Siyar al-Saghir

Key Takeaway
Al-Siyar al-Kabir is the last composed and the mu'tamad work for siyar; al-Mabsut is the asl but not always the final authority.

The Meaning of al-Usul (Zahir al-Riwayah) and al-Asl in Hanafi Works
Defining which books constitute Zahir al-Riwayah and the specific meaning of al-Asl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the books of Zahir al-Riwayah and explain the specific reference of the term al-Asl to al-Mabsut within the Hanafi textual hierarchy.

Core Idea
In Hanafi terminology, al-Usul are the six canonical works; al-Asl specifically means al-Mabsut.

In the Hanafi madhhab, not all books carry the same authority. The early scholars designated a set of works as 'al-Usul' (the principles) – also known as Zahir al-Riwayah – which form the core of reliable rulings. Among them, one book, al-Mabsut, is so foundational that it is simply called 'al-Asl'. Understanding these designations is essential for muftis to prioritize sources correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term al-Usul
Locate in the passage where it states that the books of Zahir al-Riwayah are called al-Usul. These are the six works transmitted reliably from Muhammad al-Shaybani.
Zahir al-Riwayah means 'manifest transmission' – widely known and authenticated.
2
List the six books of al-Usul
From the passage and your knowledge, list al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Mabsut, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. The passage explicitly mentions al-Jami'ayn (the two Jami's), al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut.
The Siyar books are often grouped with al-Mabsut as part of al-Usul.
3
Distinguish al-Asl from al-Usul
Note that the passage says 'al-Asl' (singular) is used specifically for al-Mabsut, not any other book. This is a terminological convention in Hanafi works.
When a Hanafi text says 'Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl', it always refers to al-Mabsut.
4
Understand the order of compilation
According to the passage, al-Mabsut was authored first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Jami' al-Kabir, then al-Ziyadat. This order is why al-Mabsut is called al-Asl.
This chronological primacy contributes to its authority.
5
Resolve the textual discrepancy
The passage clarifies that a quotation attributed to al-Bahr is actually from al-Nahr. This shows the precision expected in source referencing.
Always verify citations; misattribution can affect the reliability of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدمنا أن كتب ظاهر الرواية تسمّى بالأصول، ومنه قول "الهداية" في باب التيمم : "وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في غير رواية الأصول ". اهـ. قال الشراح: "هناك رواية الأصول : رواية الجامعين، والزيادات والمبسوط . ورواية غير الأصول : رواية النوادر والأمالي والرقيات، والكيسانيات، والهارونيات " . اهـ . وكثيراً ما يقولون : ذكره محمد في "الأصل " ، ويفسره الشراح بـ "المبسوط" ، فعلم أن الأصل مفردا، هو المبسوط، اشتهر به من بين باقى كتب الأصول. وقال في "البحر" في باب صلاة العيد (1) عن "غاية البيان" : "سمى الأصل أصلا ؛ لأنه صنف أولا، ثم الجامع الصغير، ثم الكبير، ثم الزيادات.
(١) قوله : "قال في "البحر في صلاة العيد" اعلم أن قوله : "سمى الأصل أصلا ثم الزيادات " لا يوجد في "البحر"، بل هو موجود في "النهر"، وأما قوله : "وقال : إن الجامع الصغير . . . فما فيه هو المعول عليه فموجود في "البحر" و "النهر" كليهما، لكن لا يفهم ذلك من قوله، إنما يفهم عنه أن ذلك كله عبارة "البحر"، ففى العبارة خلل واضطراب، ولو قال : "النهر " بدل "البحر " لكان أولى . ويؤيد ذلك نقله في "رد المحتار" حيث قال : وفى باب العيدين من "البحر " و "النهر " : أن الجامع الصغير صنفه محمد بعد "الأصل فما فيه هو المعول عليه، ثم قال في النهر " : "سمى الأصل أصلا؛ لأنه صنف . . . إلخ . فليتأمل . (مظ)
We have presented that the books of Zahir al-Riwayah are called al-Usul. From this is the saying of al-Hidayah in the chapter of Tayammum: 'And from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in other than the riwaya of al-Usul.' The commentators said: 'The riwaya of al-Usul: the riwaya of al-Jami'ayn (two Jami's), al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. And the riwaya of other than al-Usul: the riwaya of al-Nawadir, al-Amali, al-Ruqiyat, al-Kaysaniyat, and al-Haruniyat.' And often they say: 'Muhammad mentioned it in al-Asl,' and the commentators explain it as al-Mabsut. Thus it is known that al-Asl, in the singular, is al-Mabsut, famous among the remaining books of al-Usul. And he said in al-Bahr in the chapter of Salat al-Eid (1) from Ghayat al-Bayan: 'He named al-Asl an asl because it was authored first, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Kabir, then al-Ziyadat.' (1) His saying: 'He said in al-Bahr in Salat al-Eid:' Know that his saying: 'He named al-Asl an asl, then al-Ziyadat' is not found in al-Bahr, but rather it is found in al-Nahr. As for his saying: 'And he said: Indeed al-Jami' al-Saghir ... what is in it is relied upon' — it is found in both al-Bahr and al-Nahr, but it is not understood from his statement; rather it is understood that all that is the expression of al-Bahr. So in the expression there is defect and disorder. If he had said 'al-Nahr' instead of 'al-Bahr' it would be better. This is supported by his citation in Radd al-Muhtar where he said: 'In the chapter of the two Eids from al-Bahr and al-Nahr: that al-Jami' al-Saghir was authored by Muhammad after al-Asl, so what is in it is relied upon, then he said in al-Nahr: "He named al-Asl an asl because he authored..." etc. So let it be pondered.' (Mazhir)
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the core Hanafi textual sources. The author explains that the term 'al-Usul' (principles) refers specifically to the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, which are the six foundational works compiled by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. These include al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Mabsut, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. The term 'al-Asl' (the foundation) in singular is used specifically for al-Mabsut, the most comprehensive of these works, authored first. The passage also clarifies a textual discrepancy regarding a quotation from al-Bahr and al-Nahr, noting that the correct attribution is to al-Nahr regarding the order of compilation. This is a rasm al-mufti issue: it establishes the hierarchy of textual authority, which is essential for knowing which rulings are most relied upon in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The canonical and widely transmitted works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which are the primary sources of Hanafi rulings.
الأصل (al-Asl): Specifically refers to al-Mabsut among the books of al-Usul, as it was the first authored.
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): The comprehensive work by Muhammad al-Shaybani, the first of the Zahir al-Riwayah books and the primary reference for rulings.
الأصول (al-Usul): The plural of al-Asl; used to denote the set of Zahir al-Riwayah books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which book is referred to as 'al-Asl'?
A) Al-Jami' al-Saghir
B) Al-Mabsut
C) Al-Ziyadat
D) Al-Nawadir

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi terminology, al-Asl is the specific title for al-Mabsut, the first and foundational book of Zahir al-Riwayah, which comprises the six authoritative works of the madhhab.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Saghir-Kabir Classification: A Foundational Rasm al-Mufti Rule
Rasm al-Mufti rule with illustrative examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between saghir and kabir works of Imam Muhammad and apply this classification to determine the relative reliability of a transmitted ruling within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Saghir works carry the agreement of both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; kabir works lack that verification and are thus lower in the fatwa hierarchy.

This lesson introduces a key principle from Rasm al-Mufti: the distinction between saghir and kabir works of Imam Muhammad. Understanding this classification is essential for a mufti to weigh the authority of different transmissions. The passage provides the rule, several clarifying examples from Abu Yusuf, and a note on the special status of al-Siyar al-Kabir.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definitions
Learn that 'saghir' works were read to Abu Yusuf and agreed upon by both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, while 'kabir' works were composed solely by Muhammad without Abu Yusuf's review.
Saghir does not mean less important; it indicates a higher level of verification.
2
Identify the rule’s scope
This classification applies to all works of Imam Muhammad. It influences which riwayah (transmission) is preferred in fatwa.
The rule is from al-Bahr and commented on by Ibn Amir Haj.
3
Analyze the examples
Review the six scenarios where Abu Yusuf clarifies or corrects a narration, showing how the classification affects practical rulings.
Focus on the pattern: Abu Yusuf often limits the application of a general ruling.
4
Apply the unanimity principle
Note Ibn al-Humam's principle: if Imam Muhammad does not mention a disagreement, the ruling is the unanimous position of the early masters.
This applies to both saghir and kabir works.
5
Assess the fatwa hierarchy
Determine that saghir works are mufta bihi (operative) over kabir works when they conflict, but kabir works remain authoritative unless they contradict saghir or a stronger source.
The Siyar al-Kabir is an exception: it is the last composition and covers siyar, but it is still kabir.

الفرق بين الصغير والكبير
مطلب في الفرق بين "الصغير" و "الكبير"
وقال في "البحر" في بحث التشهد : "كل تأليف لمحمد بن الحسن موصوف بـ "الصغير"، فهو باتفاق الشيخين : أبي يوسف ومحمد بخلاف "الكبير"، فإنه لم يعرض على أبي يوسف."
وقال المحقق ابن أمير حاج الحلبي في شرحه على "المنية" في بحث قال أبو يوسف : "وإنما رويت لك حتى يدخل وقت الظهر". والثالثة : المشترى من الغاصب إذا أعتق ، ثم أجاز المالك البيع نفذ العتق، قال: "إنما رويت لك أنه لا ينفذ"
الرابعة : المهاجرة لا عدة عليها، ويجوز نكاحها إلا أن تكون حبلى، فحينئذ لا يجوز نكاحها. قال أبو يوسف : "إنما رويت لك أنه يجوز نكاحها، ولكن لا يقربها زوجها حتى تضع الحمل".
والخامسة : عبد بين اثنين قتل مولى لهما ، فعفا أحدهما، بطل الدم كله عند أبى حنيفة، وقالا : يدفع ربعه إلى شريكه أو يفديه بربع الدية، وقال أبو يوسف : "إنما حكيت لك عن أبي حنيفة، كقولنا. وإنما الاختلاف الأ"، رويته في عبد قتل مولاه عمداً، وله ابنان فعفا أحدهما . إلا أن محمداً ذكر الائتلاف فيهما، وذكر قول نفسه مع أبي يوسف في الأولى.
السادسة : رجل مات وترك ابنا له وعبدا لا غير، فادعى العبد: أن الميت كان أعتقه فى صحته، وادعى رجل على الميت ألف دينار، وقيمة العبد ألف، فقال الابن: صدقتما - يسعى العبد في قيمته وهو حر، ويأخذهما الغريم بدينه وقال أبويوسف : إنما رويت لك ما دام يسعى في قيمته أنه عبد.

وجه تصنيف السير الكبير
التسميع : إن محمداً قرأ أكثر الكتب على أبي يوسف، إلا ما كان فيه اسم الكبير، فإنه من تصنيف محمد كالمضاربة الكبير، والمزارعة الكبير، والمأذون الكبير، والجامع الكبير، والسير الكبير.
وذكر المحقق ابن الهمام كما في فتاوى تلميذه العلامة قاسم أن ما لم يحك محمد فيه خلافاً، فهو قولهم جميعاً.

مطلب في وجه تصنيف " السير الكبير "
وذكر الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسى في أول شرحه على السير الكبير : هو آخر تصنيف صنفه محمد في الفقه، ثم قال : وكان سبب تصنيفه بعد رجوعه من العراق، ولذا لم يروه عنه أبو حفص الكبير.
The difference between the small and the large. A section on the difference between 'as-saghir' and 'al-kabir'. It is said in 'al-Bahr' in the discussion on tashahhud: 'Every work of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan described as 'as-saghir' is by agreement of the two shaykhs: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Contrary to 'al-kabir', for it was not presented to Abu Yusuf.' And the investigator Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi said in his commentary on 'al-Munyah' in the discussion: Abu Yusuf said: 'I only narrated to you so that the time of Dhuhr enters.' The third: The one who buys from a usurper, if he frees the slave then the owner ratifies the sale, the emancipation is effective. He said: 'I only narrated to you that it is not effective.' The fourth: A woman who migrates has no waiting period, and her marriage is permissible unless she is pregnant, then her marriage is not permissible. Abu Yusuf said: 'I only narrated to you that her marriage is permissible, but her husband should not approach her until she delivers the child.' The fifth: A slave owned by two men killed a master of both of them, and one of the two pardoned; according to Abu Hanifa the blood-money is all dropped, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he gives one quarter to his partner or ransoms with a quarter of the blood-money. Abu Yusuf said: 'I only related to you from Abu Hanifa that it is like our statement. And the difference is that...' I narrated it regarding a slave who intentionally killed his master, and he had two sons, one of whom pardoned. Except that Muhammad mentioned the agreement in both, and he mentioned his own statement with Abu Yusuf in the first. The sixth: A man died leaving a son and a slave only, and the slave claimed that the deceased had emancipated him during his health, and a man claimed a thousand dinars against the deceased, and the value of the slave is one thousand. The son said: 'You both are truthful.' The slave works to pay his value, and he is free, and the creditor takes both for his debt. Abu Yusuf said: 'I only narrated to you that as long as he works for his value, he is a slave.'

The basis of classifying the Siyar al-Kabir. The audition: Muhammad read most of the books to Abu Yusuf, except what included the name 'al-Kabir', for it is from Muhammad's own composition, such as al-Mudarabah al-Kabir, al-Muzara'ah al-Kabir, al-Ma'dhun al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. And the investigator Ibn al-Humam mentioned, as in the fatwas of his student Allamah Qasim, that what Muhammad did not mention a difference about is the statement of all of them. A section on the basis of classifying 'al-Siyar al-Kabir'. And Imam Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in the beginning of his commentary on al-Siyar al-Kabir: it is the last work that Muhammad composed in fiqh. Then he said: The reason for its composition was after his return from Iraq, and for that reason Abu Hafs al-Kabir did not narrate it from him.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage deals with a methodological rule in Hanafi fiqh regarding the classification of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani's works. The text distinguishes two categories: 'saghir' (small) and 'kabir' (large). The rule is clear: any work by Imam Muhammad described as 'saghir' is agreed upon by the two shaykhs – Abu Yusuf and Muhammad himself – meaning the rulings in it are reliably transmitted from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf. In contrast, works described as 'kabir' were not presented to Abu Yusuf; they represent Imam Muhammad's own compilation directly from Abu Hanifa without Abu Yusuf's review. The passage then provides several examples where Abu Yusuf clarifies the transmission, often correcting a misunderstanding or specifying the exact circumstances of a ruling. These examples illustrate that Abu Yusuf's role was to verify and sometimes limit the application of certain narrations. The text then discusses the classification of the Siyar al-Kabir, noting that it is one of the 'kabir' works and is actually the last fiqh work composed by Imam Muhammad after his return from Iraq. It was not narrated by Abu Hafs al-Kabir, indicating a break in the chain of transmission. The passage also notes a general principle from Ibn al-Humam: if Imam Muhammad does not mention a disagreement in a work, then the ruling is the unanimous position of the early Hanafi masters.

Key Terms
صغير (saghir): A work of Imam Muhammad that was transmitted via Abu Yusuf and agreed upon by both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
كبير (kabir): A work of Imam Muhammad that was not presented to Abu Yusuf; it is Muhammad's own direct compilation from Abu Hanifa.
السير الكبير (al-Siyar al-Kabir): A large work by Imam Muhammad on the law of war and international relations; it is his last fiqh composition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Saghir works are smaller in volume; kabir works are larger.
B) Saghir works were read to Abu Yusuf and agreed upon; kabir works were not presented to Abu Yusuf.
C) Saghir works are only on ibadat; kabir works cover muamalat.
D) Saghir works were composed by Muhammad; kabir works by Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
The saghir-kabir classification is a key tool for Hanafi muftis to assess the reliability of Imam Muhammad's narrations.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

The Authority of Al-Mabsut: The Ultimate Source for Hanafi Fatwa
Establishing al-Mabsut as the supreme reference for Hanafi fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hierarchical priority of al-Kafi and al-Mabsut in Hanafi fatwa methodology and apply the rule that al-Mabsut overrides all other texts.

Core Idea
Al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is the most authoritative text for fatwa; no fatwa may be given contrary to it.

In the Hanafi madhhab, not all texts carry equal weight for issuing fatwas. This passage establishes a clear hierarchy: al-Kafi compiles the relied-upon narrations from Imam Muhammad, and its commentary al-Mabsut is the ultimate authority. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for a mufti to correctly determine the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the texts named
Recognize al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid and al-Mabsut by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. Note that al-Mabsut is a commentary on al-Kafi.
Al-Kafi is a collection from Zahir al-Riwayah; al-Mabsut expands and clarifies it.
2
Extract the authority rule
Find the statements that establish al-Mabsut as the final authority: 'لا يعمل بما يخالفه' (nothing contrary to it is acted upon) and 'لا يفتى إلا عليه' (no fatwa is given except by it).
These are explicit methodological rules for the mufti.
3
Understand the chain of transmission
Al-Kafi is based on the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. Al-Mabsut is its commentary, thus it carries the weight of that foundational text plus the ijtihad of al-Sarakhsi.
This gives al-Mabsut greater authority than works based on later or weaker transmissions.
4
Apply the hierarchy
When a mufti encounters a conflict between al-Mabsut and any other Hanafi text, he must give precedence to al-Mabsut. This is the relied-upon practice.
The passage emphasizes that one does not deviate from it (وليس عنه يُعدل).

Commentary on the String of Pearls of the Mufti's Rasm. Kafi al-Hakim. 21 - The strongest of its commentaries is that which is like the sun, the Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. 22 - The relied-upon of transmissions; one does not act contrary to his contrary, and one does not deviate from it. Section: Kafi al-Hakim is the collection of the speech of Muhammad in his six books which are Zahir al-Riwayah, and Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is its commentary. He said in 'Fath al-Qadir' and others: 'The book al-Kafi is the collection of the speech of Muhammad in his six books which are the books of Zahir al-Riwayah.' End. And in Sharh al-Ashbah by al-Allama Ibrahim al-Bayri: Know that among the books of legal issues (masa'il al-usul) is the book al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, and it is a relied-upon book in transmitting the madhhab; a group of shaykhs commented on it, among them Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, and it is famous as 'Mabsut'. (Mazhar). (4) His statement: 'with a word he had from among the sincere advisors' said in the chapter on Idda from Radd al-Muhtar: 'It is narrated that when Shams al-A'imma was released from prison, the Sultan married the mothers of his children to his servants.'
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage establishes the authoritative status of two key Hanafi texts: al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid and its commentary al-Mabsut by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. It begins by stating that the strongest commentary on the Kafi is the Mabsut, and that the Mabsut is the relied-upon source; one must not act contrary to it nor turn away from it. It then explains that the Kafi compiled the statements of Imam Muhammad from his six books which constitute Zahir al-Riwayah. The commentary then cites multiple sources reinforcing the primacy of the Mabsut. It includes a quote from al-Tartusi: 'The Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi: nothing contrary to it is acted upon, nothing is relied upon except it, and no fatwa is given except by it.' This is a methodological rule for muftis. It also includes praise in poetry and a biographical sketch of al-Sarakhsi, noting that he dictated the Mabsut while imprisoned in Uzjand. The passage concludes with a note about his release. The footnotes provide additional details about titles and the meaning of terms. Overall, the passage underscores that the Mabsut is the most authoritative work in the Hanafi madhhab for ifta, and that other works must be measured against it.

Key Terms
الكافي (al-Kafi): The book by al-Hakim al-Shahid that collects Imam Muhammad's statements from his six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): The commentary by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi on al-Kafi, considered the most authoritative reference for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that contain the primary transmitted positions of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is one of several equally authoritative commentaries on al-Kafi.
B) It is the strongest commentary and nothing contrary to it is acted upon.
C) It is only authoritative for issues of ibadat, not muamalat.
D) It is a secondary source to be consulted after al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya.

Key Takeaway
Al-Mabsut is the ultimate authority for fatwa in the Hanafi school; no fatwa may contradict it.

Multiple Opinions from a Mujtahid: Rule and Application
Rasm al-mufti rule on multiple opinions of a mujtahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rasm al-mufti rule that a mujtahid cannot have two contradictory opinions, explain how a later opinion revokes an earlier one, and apply this to determine the operative narration from Imam Abu Hanifa for fatwa.

Core Idea
A mujtahid's later opinion revokes the earlier; companions' selections preserve the final position.

This lesson introduces a foundational rule in Hanafi fatwa methodology: how to handle multiple narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa. You will learn the principle that a mujtahid cannot maintain two contradictory opinions, and when later opinions are known, they abrogate earlier ones. This rule is essential for a mufti to determine which narration is operative for issuing fatwas.

Guided Path
1
State the Rule
The passage states: 'It is not valid for a mujtahid to have two statements on one issue, due to contradiction.' This is the foundational principle: a single mujtahid cannot hold two contradictory opinions on the same matter simultaneously.
This prevents inconsistency in the madhhab.
2
Identify the Resolution Method
If the later of the two is known, it is considered a revocation (ruju') of the earlier, so only the later stands. If the later is not known, the later mujtahid must prefer one by the testimony of his heart (i.e., through ijtihad).
This applies to the companions of the Imam as later mujtahids.
3
Apply to Abu Hanifa's Narrations
Since multiple narrations from Abu Hanifa exist, we must determine which is later. The companions (like Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) often knew the later narrations and transmitted them, or they exercised preference. Their chosen narrations are authoritative because they reflect the Imam's final view or their calibrated ijtihad.
Thus, the mufti looks to the companions' selections as the operative positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
