⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلب يجوز اتباع الدليل وترك قول الإمام وإن وافقه أحد صاحبيه وقد علم من هذا: أنه لا خلاف في الأخذ بقول الإمام إذا وافقه أحدهما، ولذا قال الإمام قاضيخان: "وإن كانت المسألة مختلفا فيها بين أصحابنا، فإن كان مع أبي حنيفة أحد صاحبيه، يأخذ بقولهما، أي بقول الإمام ومن وافقه؛ لوفور الشرائط واستجماع أدلة الصواب فيها. وإن خالفه صاحباه في ذلك، فإن كان اختلافهم اختلاف عصر وزمان كالقضاء بظاهر العدالة، يأخذ بقول صاحبيه؛ لتغيير أحوال الناس. وفي المزارعة والمعاملة ونحوها يختار قولهما؛ لإجماع المتأخرين على ذلك. وفيما سوى ذلك يخير المفتى المجتهد، ويعمل بما أفضى إليه رأيه. وقال عبد الله بن المبارك: يأخذ بقول أبي حنيفة." اهـ. قلت: لكن قدمنا أن ما نقل عن الإمام من قوله: "إذا صح الحديث فهو مذهبي" محمول على ما لم يخرج عن المذهب بالكلية كما ظهر لنا من التقرير السابق، ومقتضاه جواز اتباع الدليل وإن خالف ما وافقه عليه أحد صاحبيه، ولهذا قال في البحر عن التتارخانية: "إذا كان الإمام في جانب، وهما في جانب خير المفتى وإن كان أحدهما مع الإمام أخذ بقولهما إلا إذا اصطلح المشايخ على قول الآخر فيتبعهم، كما اختار قوله: "أخذ بقولهما" أي بقول الإمام ومن معه من الأصحاب.
Section: It is permissible to follow the evidence and leave the Imam's saying, even if one of his two companions agrees with him. And it is known from this that there is no disagreement about adopting the Imam's saying when one of them agrees with him. Hence Imam Qadikhan said: 'If the issue is disputed among our scholars, and if one of the two companions is with Abu Hanifa, one takes their saying, meaning the Imam's saying and whoever agrees with him, due to the abundance of conditions and the gathering of evidence of correctness. If both disagree with him in that, then if their disagreement is a difference of era and time, like judging by apparent probity, he takes the saying of his two companions due to the change in people's conditions. In muzara'ah, mu'amalah, and similar matters, he chooses their saying due to the consensus of later scholars. In other than that, the mujtahid mufti is given choice, and he acts according to what his opinion leads to. And Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: He takes the saying of Abu Hanifa.' End quote. I say: But we have presented earlier that what is transmitted from the Imam that 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab' is interpreted as not going out of the madhhab entirely, as became clear to us from the previous discussion, and its consequence is the permissibility of following the evidence even if it contradicts what one of his two companions agreed with him on. Hence, it is said in al-Bahr from al-Tatarkhaniyyah: 'If the Imam is on one side and they are on the other, the mufti has choice, and if one of them is with the Imam, he takes their saying, unless the scholars have agreed on the other saying, then he follows them, as he chose...' His saying: 'He takes their saying' meaning the Imam's saying and whoever of the companions is with him.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage, from the same work, is a standalone section (mab) that expands on the rasm rule of the mufti's choice when the Sahibayn disagree. The author first asserts that when one of the Sahibayn agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa, there is no dispute: the mufti follows that combined opinion. He then quotes Qadikhan's detailed classification of four scenarios: (1) If one Sahib agrees with Imam, follow both. (2) If both disagree and the issue is time-sensitive (e.g., judging by apparent probity due to changing times), follow the Sahibayn. (3) In matters like muzara'ah (sharecropping) and mu'amalah (transactions), follow the Sahibayn due to later consensus. (4) In all other cases, the mujtahid mufti may choose. Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak is quoted as saying to follow Abu Hanifa. The author then comments (قلت) that the hadith 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab' permits following evidence even if it contradicts Imam with one Sahib. He cites al-Bahr and al-Tatarkhaniyyah to reinforce that the mufti may choose, with exceptions if the scholars have agreed on a position. This passage thus provides a more nuanced fatwa hierarchy.

Key Terms
المزارعة والمعاملة (al-muzara'ah wa al-mu'amalah): Sharecropping and financial transactions, where custom ('urf) is given weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Qadikhan, in which of the following cases does the mufti take the saying of the two companions (Sahibayn) even if they both disagree with Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) In all cases
B) In matters where they differ on a purely textual issue
C) In matters of custom and transactions like muzara'ah
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Qadikhan's scenarios provide a practical hierarchy: the mufti must classify the dispute into one of four categories before deciding which opinion to follow.

Following Evidence Over Imam: Scope and Limits
Author's comment on permissibility of following evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that a mufti may follow authentic hadith over the Imam's saying, provided it does not contradict the madhhab entirely, and apply this principle to mufti choice scenarios.

Core Idea
Authentic hadith can override Imam's opinion, but never exit the madhhab entirely.

After presenting Qadikhan's scenarios, the author adds a crucial refinement: the mufti is not bound to follow the Imam when an authentic hadith contradicts him, as per the Imam's own statement. This lesson explores the limits of that principle and how it interacts with the fatwa hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's main claim in his comment (قلت)
Read the author's words: 'But we have presented earlier that what is transmitted from the Imam that 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab' is interpreted as not going out of the madhhab entirely.'
The key is 'not going out of the madhhab entirely.'
2
Understand the condition: 'not going out of the madhhab entirely'
This means the mufti cannot follow an interpretation that contradicts the fundamental principles (usul) of the Hanafi school, even if a hadith seems to support it.
Example: if a hadith seems to reject qiyas, Hanafis do not follow it because qiyas is an usul of the school.
3
Apply to Qadikhan's scenarios
Consider a case where one Sahib agrees with Imam but an authentic hadith suggests otherwise. The author says the mufti may follow the hadith, overriding the combined opinion.
But this is only if the hadith can be incorporated within the madhhab framework.
4
Reference the citation from al-Bahr and al-Tatarkhaniyyah
The author quotes that if Imam is on one side and Sahibayn on the other, the mufti has choice; if one Sahib agrees with Imam, he takes their saying unless scholars have agreed on the other saying.
This reinforces that consensus can overrule the hadith principle.
5
Synthesize: when can the mufti follow evidence?
The mufti can follow evidence when it is authentic and can be reconciled with the madhhab's usul, and when there is no definitive contrary consensus. If later scholars have agreed on a position, that consensus prevails.
This shows a layered authority: hadith > Imam's opinion (with conditions) > later consensus.

مطلب يجوز اتباع الدليل وترك قول الإمام وإن وافقه أحد صاحبيه وقد علم من هذا: أنه لا خلاف في الأخذ بقول الإمام إذا وافقه أحدهما، ولذا قال الإمام قاضيخان: "وإن كانت المسألة مختلفا فيها بين أصحابنا، فإن كان مع أبي حنيفة أحد صاحبيه، يأخذ بقولهما، أي بقول الإمام ومن وافقه؛ لوفور الشرائط واستجماع أدلة الصواب فيها. وإن خالفه صاحباه في ذلك، فإن كان اختلافهم اختلاف عصر وزمان كالقضاء بظاهر العدالة، يأخذ بقول صاحبيه؛ لتغيير أحوال الناس. وفي المزارعة والمعاملة ونحوها يختار قولهما؛ لإجماع المتأخرين على ذلك. وفيما سوى ذلك يخير المفتى المجتهد، ويعمل بما أفضى إليه رأيه. وقال عبد الله بن المبارك: يأخذ بقول أبي حنيفة." اهـ. قلت: لكن قدمنا أن ما نقل عن الإمام من قوله: "إذا صح الحديث فهو مذهبي" محمول على ما لم يخرج عن المذهب بالكلية كما ظهر لنا من التقرير السابق، ومقتضاه جواز اتباع الدليل وإن خالف ما وافقه عليه أحد صاحبيه، ولهذا قال في البحر عن التتارخانية: "إذا كان الإمام في جانب، وهما في جانب خير المفتى وإن كان أحدهما مع الإمام أخذ بقولهما إلا إذا اصطلح المشايخ على قول الآخر فيتبعهم، كما اختار قوله: "أخذ بقولهما" أي بقول الإمام ومن معه من الأصحاب.
Section: It is permissible to follow the evidence and leave the Imam's saying, even if one of his two companions agrees with him. And it is known from this that there is no disagreement about adopting the Imam's saying when one of them agrees with him. Hence Imam Qadikhan said: 'If the issue is disputed among our scholars, and if one of the two companions is with Abu Hanifa, one takes their saying, meaning the Imam's saying and whoever agrees with him, due to the abundance of conditions and the gathering of evidence of correctness. If both disagree with him in that, then if their disagreement is a difference of era and time, like judging by apparent probity, he takes the saying of his two companions due to the change in people's conditions. In muzara'ah, mu'amalah, and similar matters, he chooses their saying due to the consensus of later scholars. In other than that, the mujtahid mufti is given choice, and he acts according to what his opinion leads to. And Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: He takes the saying of Abu Hanifa.' End quote. I say: But we have presented earlier that what is transmitted from the Imam that 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab' is interpreted as not going out of the madhhab entirely, as became clear to us from the previous discussion, and its consequence is the permissibility of following the evidence even if it contradicts what one of his two companions agreed with him on. Hence, it is said in al-Bahr from al-Tatarkhaniyyah: 'If the Imam is on one side and they are on the other, the mufti has choice, and if one of them is with the Imam, he takes their saying, unless the scholars have agreed on the other saying, then he follows them, as he chose...' His saying: 'He takes their saying' meaning the Imam's saying and whoever of the companions is with him.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage, from the same work, is a standalone section (mab) that expands on the rasm rule of the mufti's choice when the Sahibayn disagree. The author first asserts that when one of the Sahibayn agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa, there is no dispute: the mufti follows that combined opinion. He then quotes Qadikhan's detailed classification of four scenarios: (1) If one Sahib agrees with Imam, follow both. (2) If both disagree and the issue is time-sensitive (e.g., judging by apparent probity due to changing times), follow the Sahibayn. (3) In matters like muzara'ah (sharecropping) and mu'amalah (transactions), follow the Sahibayn due to later consensus. (4) In all other cases, the mujtahid mufti may choose. Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak is quoted as saying to follow Abu Hanifa. The author then comments (قلت) that the hadith 'If the hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab' permits following evidence even if it contradicts Imam with one Sahib. He cites al-Bahr and al-Tatarkhaniyyah to reinforce that the mufti may choose, with exceptions if the scholars have agreed on a position. This passage thus provides a more nuanced fatwa hierarchy.

Key Terms
المزارعة والمعاملة (al-muzara'ah wa al-mu'amalah): Sharecropping and financial transactions, where custom ('urf) is given weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what condition must be met for a mufti to follow an authentic hadith that contradicts Imam Abu Hanifa and one Sahib?
A) The hadith must be mutawatir
B) The hadith must not cause the mufti to leave the madhhab entirely
C) The hadith must have been accepted by all Sahibayn
D) The mufti must have permission from a senior scholar

Key Takeaway
The mufti may follow authentic hadith over the Imam and one Sahib, provided the alternative remains within the Hanafi framework, but later consensus can override even this principle.

When the Mufti May Prefer the Two Companions Over the Imam
Rule for mufti on when to prefer the two companions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi jurisprudential hierarchy to determine when a mufti may prefer the opinion of the two companions over Imam Abu Hanifa, citing the evidence of ijma and changed circumstances.

Core Idea
A mufti may prefer the two companions' opinions in justice and transactions due to ijma and changing needs, with discretion in other matters.

This passage presents a critical rule for muftis: navigating between the Imam's opinion and his two main disciples. It clarifies that preference is not arbitrary but guided by evidence, consensus of later scholars, and practical realities. The author both states a general principle and refines it with detailed conditions, making it essential for any mufti operating within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule for justice matters
The passage begins: 'In matters of justice, he takes the opinion of his two companions due to the change of people's circumstances.' Note that the mufti here is assumed to be a mujtahid capable of preferring opinions.
Justice matters include court judgments and similar rulings where social context matters.
2
Specify the exceptions for financial transactions
In sharecropping (muzara'ah) and capital partnership (mu'amalah), the companions' opinion is explicitly chosen due to the consensus (ijma) of later scholars. This is a stronger directive than the general rule.
These two areas are explicitly named; 'similar matters' may include other contemporary transactions.
3
Understand the mufti's choice in other matters
In all other cases, the mujtahid mufti has a choice and acts according to his own preference. This is not arbitrary but is guided by the Imam's principle that following authentic hadith is paramount.
The mufti must still stay within the madhhab's boundaries, as clarified by the author's commentary.
4
Analyze the proof from al-Tatarkhaniyya
When the Imam and both companions are on opposite sides, the mufti has choice. But if one companion sides with the Imam, the mufti normally follows the two companions (majority). However, if later mashayikh have agreed on the other opinion, he follows them.
This is a layered approach: majority view of the immediate disciples is preferred, but later consensus can override.
5
Apply the lesson to a practical scenario
Imagine a modern case of joint venture (mudaraba). The later Hanafi scholars have largely followed the two companions on conditions of profit-sharing. A mufti should therefore adopt their view, even if Imam Abu Hanifa's original opinion was different.
This shows the importance of tracking later fatwa trends within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم مخالفة الصاحبين الإمام العدالة، يأخذ بقول صاحبيه ؛ لتغيير أحوال الناس. وفي المزارعة والمعاملة ونحوها يختار قولهما ؛ لإجماع المتأخرين على ذلك . وفيما سوى ذلك يخير المفتى المجتهد، ويعمل بما أفضى إليه رأيه . وقال عبد الله بن المبارك : يأخذ بقول أبي حنيفة . قلت : لكن قدمنا أن ما نقل عن الإمام من قوله : "إذا صح الحديث فهو مذهبي ، محمول على ما لم يخرج عن المذهب بالكلية كما ظهر لنا من التقرير السابق، ومقتضاه جواز اتباع الدليل وإن خالف ما وافقه عليه أحد صاحبيه، ولهذا قال في البحر عن التتارخانية : "إذا كان الإمام في جانب، وهما في جانب خير المفتى وإن كان أحدهما مع الإمام أخذ بقولهما إلا إذا اصطلح المشايخ على قول الآخر فيتبعهم، كما اختار الفقيه أبو الليث قول زفر في مسائل ."
The ruling on contradicting the two companions: In matters of justice, he takes the opinion of his two companions due to the change of people's circumstances. In sharecropping, capital partnership, and similar matters, he chooses their opinion due to the consensus of the later scholars. In other than that, the mujtahid mufti has a choice and acts according to what his opinion leads him to. Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: 'He takes the opinion of Abu Hanifa.' I say: But we have established that what has been transmitted from the Imam, 'When a hadith is authentic, that is my madhhab', is interpreted as long as it does not depart from the madhhab entirely, as became clear from the previous explanation. Its implication is the permissibility of following the evidence even if it contradicts what one of his two companions agreed with him on. Therefore, it is said in al-Bahr from al-Tatarkhaniyya: 'When the Imam is on one side and the two companions are on another, the mufti has a choice, but if one of them is with the Imam, he takes the opinion of both (i.e., the two companions), unless the mashayikh have agreed upon the other opinion, then he follows them, as Abu al-Layth chose the opinion of Zufar in some issues.'
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (hukm) from the discourse on the mufti's methodology. It begins by stating a general principle: in matters of justice ('adalat) – such as court judgments – the mufti should take the opinion of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) over the Imam's opinion when people's circumstances have changed. Then it specifies that in financial transactions like muzara'ah (sharecropping) and mu'amalah (partnership), the companions' opinion is chosen due to the consensus (ijma') of later scholars. In all other matters, the mufti who is a mujtahid (capable of ijtihad) is free to choose the opinion he prefers. The author then quotes Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak who holds the opposite view: always take Abu Hanifa's opinion. The author clarifies with his own commentary ('qultu') that the Imam's famous statement 'When a hadith is authentic, that is my madhhab' implies that following the evidence is paramount, even if it contradicts the Imam's stated position and even if one of the companions agreed with him. The author supports this by citing a passage from al-Bahr quoting al-Tatarkhaniyya: when the Imam and the two companions differ, the mufti has choice; but if one companion sides with the Imam, the mufti normally adopts the opinion of the two companions (the majority), unless the later mashayikh (authorities) have agreed upon the other opinion, in which case he follows them. An example is Abu al-Layth choosing the view of Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a companion of Abu Hanifa, in certain matters. Thus, this passage teaches that the mufti's discretion is guided by evidence, custom, need, and the consensus of later scholars, not mere personal preference.

Key Terms
الصاحبين (al-sahibayn): The two main disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
المفتى المجتهد (al-mufti al-mujtahid): A mufti capable of ijtihad within the madhhab (i.e., not an absolute mujtahid but one who can weigh and prefer opinions).
إجماع المتأخرين (ijma' al-muta'akhkhirin): Consensus of later Hanafi scholars (approximately from the 6th century onwards).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which types of cases does the mufti choose the opinion of the two companions over the Imam?
A) In all matters of worship ('ibadat).
B) In matters of justice and transactions like sharecropping and partnership.
C) Only when the Imam's evidence is weak.
D) Only when a later scholar's consensus exists.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must balance the Imam's original opinion with the consensus of later scholars and changing circumstances, especially in financial transactions where the two companions' view is preferred.

The Mufti's Duty to Follow Tafsil and Corrections
Rasm rule on mufti's duty to follow tafsil and corrections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a later Hanafi mufti must follow the tafsil (ranking of imams) and identify when an early scholar's correction (tasḥīḥ) overrides the default order.

Core Idea
A later mufti cannot prefer by evidence; he is bound by the ranking of imams unless early scholars corrected it.

This passage defines the mufti's limits in later times. After the era of mujtahids, a mufti is a pure muqallid. He must follow the detailed ranking of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa first, then Abu Yusuf, etc.), unless the early mujtahids of the school have corrected a position due to stronger evidence or changed circumstances. You will learn how to identify the tafsil and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufti's era
The passage distinguishes between the classical era (when mujtahidun fi al-madhhab existed) and the later era (when only pure muqallids remain). Determine which era applies to the mufti in question.
In our time, all muftis are considered later-era muqallids.
2
Understand the tafsil principle
The tafsil is the fixed order for giving fatwa: first the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani, and so on. This is the default hierarchy.
This order is based on the rank of the imams in the madhhab.
3
Recognize the exception
If the early scholars (mujtahidun fi al-madhhab) have corrected (ṣaḥḥaḥū) a ruling contrary to the tafsil, the mufti must follow that corrected ruling. The correction may be due to strength of evidence, change of circumstances, or other valid reasons.
Such corrections are found in the works of later authorities like Ibn Abidin.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a case where Abu Hanifa says X, Abu Yusuf says Y, and early scholars corrected to Y, the mufti gives fatwa with Y. If no correction exists, he follows the tafsil (first Abu Hanifa).
5
Verify with historical examples
The passage mentions that Imam Zufar's sayings were preferred in seventeen (later twenty) specific positions. This illustrates that corrections are limited and documented.
Students should consult works like Radd al-Muhtar for such lists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة في المراد بالاجتهاد هنا في المذهب (١) ، وعرف بأنه : المتمكن من تخريج الوجوه على منصوص إمامه، أو المتبحر في مذهب إمامه المتمكن من ترجيح قول له على آخر أطلقه" . اهـ. وسيأتي توضیحه. ۳۰- فَالآنَ لا تَرْجِيْحَ بالدليل فَلَيْسَ إِلا الْقَوْلُ بالتفصيل) -٣١ مَا لَمْ يَكُن خلافُهُ المُصحح (۳) فَنَاخُذُ - (٣) فَنأخُذُ الذى لهم قد وضـ وَضَحَا ٣٢- فَإِنَّنَا نَرَاهُمُوا قَدْ رَجَحُوا مَقَالَ بَعْضٍ صَحْبِهِ وَصَحْحُوا ٣٣- مِنْ ذَاكَ مَا قَدْ رَجَحُوا لِزُفَرُ مَقَالَهُ فِي سَبْعَةٍ وَعَشَرْ والترجيح، وأصحاب التصحيح . وقد أشرنا إليه من قبل، ثم هذا كله في زمانهم، أما في زماننا الذى انقطع فيه المجتهدون بأنواعهم ولم يبق إلا المقلد المحض، لا سبيل إلا إلى الأخذ بأقوال الأئمة بالترتيب ما لم يصرح المشايخ بخلافه، كما يأتي . وقوله : " وهو المجتهد في المذهب أى وهو اجتهاد المجتهد في المذهب، فالكلام على حذف المضاف . (۱) قوله : وهو المجتهد في المذهب أى وهو اجتهاد المجتهد في المذهب، فالكلام على حذف المضاف . (۲) قوله : " فليس إلا القول بالتفصيل "ليس " تامة، والاستثناء مفرغ. والمراد من التفصيل هو الترتيب بين أقوال أئمة المذهب، المذكور قبل بيتين . (۳) قوله : " ما لم يكن خلافه المصححات الفعل الناقص تام و المصححا صفة "خلافه"، وبدل رفعه إلى النصب للضرورة الشعرية، والموصوف مع الصفة فاعل لم يكن " ، أى ما لم يوجد القول المصحح المخالف للتفصيل المار في الشعر السادس والعشرين والسابع والعشرين. 21 تتمة في المراد بالاجتهاد هنا مطلب ليس للمفتى في زماننا التخيير والترجيح بل عليه أن يتبع أهل الترجيح والتصحيح قد علمت أن الأصح تخيير المفتي المجتهد، فيفتى بما يكون دليله أقوى، ولا يلزمه المشى على التفصيل. ولما انقطع المفتى المجتهد في زماننا ولم يبق إلا المقلد المحض، وجب علينا اتباع التفصيل، فنفتى أولا بقول الإمام ثم وثم، ما لم نو المجتهدين في المذهب صححوا خلافه؛ لقوة دليله، أو لتغيّر الزمان، أو نحو ذلك مما يظهر لهم، فنتبع ما قالوا كما لو كانوا أحياء وأفتونا بذلك، كما علمته آنفًا من كلام العلامة قاسم ؛ لأنهم أعلم وأدرى بالمذهب، وعلى هذا عملهم، فإننا رأيناهم قد يرجحون قول صاحبيه تارة، وقول أحدهما تارةً، وتارةً قول زفر في سبعة عشر موضعا (۱) ، ذكرها البيري في رسالة، ولسيدى أحمد الحموي منظومة في ذلك، لكن بعض مسائلها مستدرك ؛ لكونه لم يختص به زفر . وقد نظمت في ذلك منظومة فريدة أسقطت منها ما هو مستدرك، وزدت على ما نظمه الحموي عدة مسائل، وقد ذكرت هذه المنظومة (٢) في حاشيتي "رد المحتار " من باب النفقة (۱) قوله : "في سبعة عشر موضعاً قال في رد المحتار في باب النفقة ما ملخصه : " أفضلها الحموى إلى خمس عشرة مسألة ونظمها في قصيدة، ويجب إسقاط ثلاثة منها وهى : دعوى العقار، وشهادة الأعمى والوصية بثلث النقد، كما نبه عليه سيدى عبد الغني النابلسي في شرحه على النظم المذكور، وقد زدت على ذلك ثماني ،مسائل فصارت جملة المسائل عشرين مسألة بعد إسقاط الثلاثة المارة" ، انتهى ملخصاً. (٦٠٨،٦٠٧/٣) (۲) قوله : " ذكرت هذه المنظومة " ذكرها في المجلد الثالث تشتمل على عشرين بيتًا
Completion regarding the intended meaning of ijtihad here in the madhhab. It is defined as: one who is capable of deriving aspects from the texts of his imam, or one who is deeply learned in the madhhab of his imam, able to prefer one of his statements over another. End. Its explanation will come. 30- So now there is no preferring by evidence; there is only the saying with detail (tafsil) 31- unless there exists a corrected (statement) contrary to it, then we take what they (the early scholars) have clearly preferred. 32- For we see that they have preferred the saying of some of his (Abu Hanifa's) companions and corrected (it). 33- Among that is what they have preferred for Zufar, his saying in seventeen places. And tarjih and the people of correction. We have indicated this before. Then all of this was in their time. As for our time, in which the mujtahids of all types have ended and nothing remains except the pure muqallid, there is no way except to take the sayings of the imams in order, unless the early scholars (mashayikh) have explicitly stated otherwise, as will come. And his saying: 'He is the mujtahid in the madhhab' meaning it is the ijtihad of the mujtahid in the madhhab; the speech is with the elision of the genitive. (1) His saying: 'He is the mujtahid in the madhhab' meaning it is the ijtihad of the mujtahid in the madhhab; the speech is with the elision of the genitive. (2) His saying: 'There is only the saying with detail' – 'laysa' is complete (tamma), and the exception is mufarrag. The intended meaning of 'tafsil' is the order between the sayings of the imams of the madhhab, mentioned two verses earlier. (3) His saying: 'Unless there exists a corrected contrary to it' – the incomplete verb 'yakun' is complete (tam), and 'al-musahhaha' is an attribute of 'khilafahu'; and the raising of it is changed to nasb due to poetic necessity; the described with the attribute is the subject of 'yakun'; i.e., unless there exists the corrected saying contrary to the tafsil mentioned in the 26th and 27th verses. 21 Completion regarding ijtihad here: A subject: The mufti in our time does not have choice (takhayyur) and preference (tarjih); rather, he must follow the people of preference and correction. You have learned that the soundest view is that the mujtahid mufti may choose, giving fatwa based on what is strongest in evidence, and he is not required to follow the tafsil. But when the mujtahid mufti has ended in our time and nothing remains except the pure muqallid, it became obligatory upon us to follow the tafsil. So we first give fatwa by the saying of the Imam, then next, unless we see that the mujtahids in the madhhab have corrected contrary to it due to strength of evidence, or due to change of time, or something similar that appears to them; then we follow what they said, as if they were alive and gave us fatwa with that, as you have just learned from the speech of Allama Qasim. Because they are most knowledgeable and most aware of the madhhab, and upon this is their practice. For we have seen that they sometimes prefer the saying of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), sometimes the saying of one of them, and sometimes the saying of Zufar in seventeen places (1), mentioned by al-Biri in a treatise; and Sayyid Ahmad al-Hamawi has a poem about that, but some of its issues are questionable because they are not exclusive to Zufar. I have composed a unique poem, dropping what is questionable and adding several issues to what al-Hamawi versified; I have mentioned this poem (2) in my margin note 'Radd al-Muhtar' in the chapter of Nafaqah. (1) His saying: 'in seventeen places' – said in Radd al-Muhtar in the chapter of Nafaqah, summarizing: 'al-Hamawi listed fifteen issues and versified them in a qasida, and three must be dropped: the claim of real estate, the testimony of a blind person, and the bequest of one-third of cash, as pointed out by Sayyid Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulusi in his commentary on the mentioned poem; and I added eight issues, making the total twenty issues after dropping the three mentioned.' End summary. (608,607/3) (2) His saying: 'I mentioned this poem' – he mentioned it in the third volume containing twenty verses.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule defining the duty of the mufti in later times regarding ijtihad and tarjih within the Hanafi madhhab. The author first clarifies that the true mujtahid within the madhhab is one who can derive rulings from the imam's texts or prefer one saying over another. However, this ability has disappeared; now only the pure muqallid remains. Therefore, the mufti cannot exercise free choice (takhayyur) or preference (tarjih) based on evidence; rather, he must follow the detailed ranking (tafsil) of the imams' sayings: first Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, and so on. This rule has an exception: if the early scholars (mujtahidun fi al-madhhab) have corrected the tafsil by preferring a different saying due to stronger evidence, changed circumstances, or other valid reasons, then the mufti must follow that correction. The author illustrates this with the case of Imam Zufar, whose sayings were preferred in seventeen (later twenty) specific positions, as compiled by later scholars. The mufti's duty is passive: he does not create preferences but implements those established by the early authorities.

Key Terms
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab): One who is able to derive rulings from the texts of his imam or to prefer one of the imam's sayings over another.
التفصيل (al-tafsil): The detailed ranking of the sayings of the Hanafi imams in order: first Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani, etc.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Preference given to one saying over another based on strength of evidence or other valid grounds.
المقلد المحض (al-muqallid al-mahd): A pure imitator who has no capability of ijtihad or tarjih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary duty of the mufti in our time regarding conflicting rulings in the Hanafi school?
A) He may choose any ruling based on his own analysis of evidence.
B) He must follow the detailed ranking (tafsil) of imams unless the early scholars have corrected it.
C) He must only follow the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa.
D) He must seek a fatwa from a living mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi mufti is a pure muqallid who must adhere to the tafsil ranking of imams unless the early scholars have made a correction.

The Hierarchy of Fatwa: When to Follow Imam Abu Hanifa
Response to the claim that it is obligatory to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion unconditionally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy and identify when a mufti must follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion versus when a mujtahid may depart from it based on proof strength.

Core Idea
A muqallid must follow the Imam; a mujtahid follows the stronger proof.

This passage addresses a critical question in Hanafi fatwa methodology: is a mufti always bound by Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, even if he finds a stronger contradictory proof? The author of al-Bahr argued for unconditional adherence, but the classical answer is more nuanced. Through analysis of the mashayikh's practice and Imam's own directives, this lesson will equip you to navigate the hierarchy between taqlid and ijtihad within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the challenge
Read the opening claim from al-Bahr: 'It is obligatory for us to give fatwa according to the statement of the Imam even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it.' Understand the problem: how can later scholars (mashayikh) depart from the Imam's opinion if they are muqallids?
This is the common tension between strict taqlid and practical ijtihad.
2
Examine the initial answer
The text first reports a transmitted answer: the mashayikh deviated because they lacked knowledge of the Imam's proof (dalil). Since the Imam set a condition that one must know his proof to give fatwa, the condition was absent for them.
This answer implies the mashayikh were unaware of the proof, which is weak.
3
Analyze the correct answer
The commentator (sharh) provides a better explanation: the mashayikh actually followed the Imam's own commands—to follow authentic hadith and to consider the strength of proof. Their departure was based on stronger evidence, not ignorance. They were capable of evaluating proofs (ahl al-nazar).
Key evidence: 'If a hadith is authentic, it is my madhhab.'
4
Apply the hierarchy
The passage concludes that in early times, knowing the proof was a condition; later, preservation (hifz) suffices for non-mujtahids. Thus: for a muqallid mufti, following the Imam is obligatory; for a mujtahid mufti, he may prefer the stronger proof after evaluation.
Ibn al-Humam is cited as an example of a mujtahid who could deviate if proof was weak.

A section on responding to what the author of 'al-Bahr' said: 'It is obligatory for us to give fatwa according to the statement of the Imam even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it.' And he said in 'al-Bahr' from the book of al-Qada': 'If you say: How is it permissible for the mashayikh to give fatwa according to other than the statement of the greatest Imam when they are muqallids? I say: This was problematic for a long time, and I did not see an answer to it except what I now understand from their words, which is that they transmitted from our companions: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said it.' Its first part: With praise of the Lord of the worlds, beginning with basmala, I adorn my poetry and prayer upon the Most High, and then: None gives fatwa according to what Zufar said except in twenty forms whose division is clear. (1) His saying: 'which is that they transmitted' - al-Ramli said: This is narrated from the mashayikh, as is apparent from its context. (2) His saying: 'until he knows from where we said it?' i.e., as long as he does not know its source from the Book, the Sunnah, the consensus of the Ummah, or obvious and hidden analogy in the matter. The gist of this answer is that the statement of our companions obligated the mashayikh not to give fatwa according to the statement of the Imam except after knowing his proof, so their giving fatwa contrary to his statement is interpreted as their not having come across his proof, and in their case the condition of the permissibility of giving fatwa according to his statement is absent. But the correct answer to this problem is what the commentator points to: that the mashayikh acted upon his command: 'If a proof comes to you, then speak according to it,' and upon his statement: 'If a hadith is authentic, then it is my madhhab,' and upon his recommendation: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said it' because the meaning of this speech is that they should look at his proof and consider its strength, so their deviation from his statement and giving fatwa according to other than it is due to this, not that they did not come across his proof; because their books are filled with proofs, and one should not think that they were ignorant of the proof of the madhhab of their Imam and gave preference to some statements over others without looking at the proofs. The capacity for ijtihad and fatwa, until it is narrated in al-Sirajiyya: This is the reason for the opposition of ‘Isam to the Imam, and he used to give fatwa contrary to his statement frequently because he did not know the proof, and another proof would appear to him so he would give fatwa according to it. So I say: This condition was in their time. As for our time, preservation (memorization) suffices as in al-Quniyah and others, so it is permissible to give fatwa according to the Imam's statement, rather it is obligatory, even if we do not know from where he said it. And based on this, what he verified in al-Hawi - i.e., that consideration is for the strength of the proof - is built upon that condition, and they verified that giving fatwa according to the Imam's statement (is valid). So the result is: that it is obligatory for us to give fatwa according to the Imam's statement even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it, because they only gave fatwa contrary to it due to the absence of the condition on their part, which is knowing his proof. As for us, we have the permission to give fatwa even if we do not know his proof. And it occurred to the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in several places: refutation of the mashayikh in giving fatwa according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that one does not deviate from his (Imam's) statement except due to weakness of his proof. But he is capable of ijtihad in the proof, while whoever is not capable of ijtihad in it must give fatwa according to the Imam's statement.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti discussion addressing a challenge raised by the author of al-Bahr: if the Hanafi school requires following Imam Abu Hanifa, how can later scholars (mashayikh) give fatwa contrary to his opinion? The text presents the earlier response that the mashayikh acted according to the condition that one must know the proof behind the Imam's ruling. They concluded that the mashayikh must have lacked knowledge of the proof, thus justifying their deviation. However, the commentator (sharh) provides a more precise answer: the mashayikh followed the Imam's own instructions to follow authentic proof and to consider the strength of evidence. Therefore, their preference for other opinions was based on stronger proof, not ignorance. The text then notes that in earlier times this condition (knowing the proof) was required, but in later times, mere memorization suffices, and it becomes obligatory to follow the Imam's opinion even without knowing the proof. Ibn al-Humam's position is cited: he had the capacity for ijtihad and could deviate if proof was weak, but for those not capable, following the Imam is obligatory. This establishes a hierarchy: for mujtahids, evaluation of proof is valid; for muqallids, adherence to Imam's opinion is required.

Key Terms
مشايخ (mashayikh): Later Hanafi jurists who sometimes differed from Imam Abu Hanifa in their fatwas.
الإمام (al-imam): Imam Abu Hanifa (d. 150 AH), the eponym of the Hanafi school.
دليل (dalil): Proof or evidence from Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Qiyas (jali and khafi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a mujtahid to prefer stronger proof over the Imam's opinion, but a muqallid must follow the Imam's ruling.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation to Follow Imam Abu Hanifa in Fatwa
Ruling on the obligation to follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position that a mufti must give fatwa by Imam Abu Hanifa's statement even without knowing the evidence, and evaluate the contrary position based on the madhhab's historical development.

Core Idea
After the madhhab's establishment, following the Imam's opinion is obligatory, not optional.

The Hanafi school has a clear hierarchy for issuing fatwa. A key question is whether a mufti must personally know the evidence for a ruling before he can issue it. This passage from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti addresses that question directly, resolving the tension between an earlier requirement and the later practice of the school. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for anyone who will issue fatwa or study Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical condition
The passage begins with a report from al-Sirajiyyah: 'Isam used to give fatwa contrary to the Imam because he did not know the evidence, and another evidence would appear to him.' This shows that knowing the Imam's evidence was once considered a condition.
The condition applied to early scholars who could engage in ijtihad.
2
Recognize the shift in the later school
The author explicitly states: 'This condition existed in their time. As for our time, it suffices with memorization... so giving fatwa by the Imam's statement is permissible, rather obligatory, even if we do not know from where he said.'
The shift is based on the madhhab's codification.
3
Understand the exception for qualified scholars
Ibn al-Humam, being 'ahl al-nazar' (qualified to examine evidence), could deviate from the Imam's statement if the evidence for another opinion is stronger. But for others, deviation is not allowed.
This is a key hierarchy: only mujtahids within the madhhab can prefer other opinions based on evidence.
4
Reconcile the apparent contradiction with the Imam's own words
Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak quoted the Imam saying: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said it.' The author gives two answers: either this was for those who could directly access the evidence, or it applied before the madhhab's compilation.
The relied-upon position is that this condition no longer applies.
5
Apply the rule
Thus, for a mufti today, following the Imam's statement is obligatory. Even if some mashayikh gave fatwa contrary, they did so because they lacked the condition of knowing the Imam's evidence in their own capacity. We follow the Imam without needing to verify the evidence.
This is the mufta bihi position for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Explanation of contracts of the mufti: Qualification for consideration and fatwa. Even transmitted in al-Sirajiyyah: 'Indeed this is the reason for the opposition of Isam to the Imam, and he used to give fatwa contrary to his statement often, because he did not know the evidence, and another evidence would appear to him, so he would give fatwa by it.' So I say: This condition existed in their time. As for our time, it suffices with memorization as in al-Qunyah and others, so giving fatwa by the Imam's statement is permissible, rather obligatory, even if we do not know from where he said? And upon this, what he corrected in al-Hawi — i.e., that consideration is for the strength of evidence — is based on that condition. And they have corrected that giving fatwa is by the Imam's statement. So the result from this is: it is obligatory upon us to give fatwa by the Imam's statement even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it, because they only gave fatwa contrary to it due to the loss of the condition in their own right, which is standing on his evidence. As for us, we have the right to give fatwa even if we have not stood on his evidence. ... And it occurred to the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in places to refute the mashayikh regarding giving fatwa by the opinion of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), saying: 'One does not deviate from his statement except due to weakness of his evidence... but he is qualified for consideration of the evidence. And whoever is not qualified for consideration of it, then upon him is to give fatwa by the Imam's statement.' Section on the meaning of qualification for consideration and fatwa. (1) And what is meant by qualification here (2) is that he be knowledgeable, distinguishing between opinions, having the ability to... (1) His statement: 'But he is qualified for consideration' is a qualification with regard to his statement: 'One does not deviate from his statement except due to weakness of his evidence' meaning that someone like the muhaqqiq can say that because he is qualified for consideration of the evidence. As for someone like us, it is not permissible for him to deviate from the Imam's statement at all. The gist of this qualification is that the 'allamah himself considered the strength of the evidence, so it is known from it that giving fatwa by the Imam's statement is not obligatory. He answered that he is qualified for consideration of the evidence, so he may deviate from the Imam's statement if his consideration requires that, but this is not permissible for others. (2) His statement: 'What is meant by qualification here' is from the words of the author of al-Bahr. Its summary: that the people of knowledge and fatwa are those who have the faculty — meaning the ability to acquire knowledge and answer — and consideration is not given in it to the actual recall of issues and answering; rather, the ahl of a thing is the one fitted for it and prepared for it with a near readiness, not the one for whom that thing has been obtained and is present with him actually. (1) His statement: 'And this is carried upon...' repels an anticipated objection. Its explanation: that Imam Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak made knowledge of hadith and qiyas — i.e., knowledge of the evidences of statements — a condition for permissibility of giving fatwa. According to this, it is not permissible to give fatwa without knowledge of the evidence? This contradicts what the author of al-Bahr claimed earlier with his statement: 'As for us, we said we give fatwa by the Imam's statement even if we have not stood on his evidence.' He answered with two answers: First: our companions differed about the permissibility of fatwa for one who does not know the evidence and its impermissibility. The statement of Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak is based on the second narration. Second: what Imam Ibn al-Mubarak said about the necessity of knowing the evidence is carried on the time before the codification, refinement, and editing of the madhhab. As for now, there is no need to know the evidences and then prefer the statement of someone other than the Imam due to strength of evidence. Rather, we must imitate the Imam, and give fatwa upon his statement, and judge by his madhhab, even if we do not know his source. (2) His statement: 'his commentator objected' i.e., the commentator of al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the qualification of a mufti and the obligation to follow the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa. It begins by discussing a historical example: 'Isam used to give fatwa contrary to the Imam because he knew a different evidence. The author explains that the condition of knowing the evidence existed in earlier times, but in our time it suffices to memorize the rulings. Thus, it is permissible and even obligatory to give fatwa by the Imam's statement without knowing his evidence. The author then addresses an apparent contradiction: the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam, being qualified to examine evidence, could deviate from the Imam's statement if the evidence for another opinion is stronger. However, for those not qualified, they must follow the Imam. The text then defines 'ahliyyah' (qualification) as the capacity and readiness to issue fatwa, not actual recall of all issues. A quote from Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak is reconciled: his requirement of knowing evidence applies before the madhhab's codification; now we simply follow the Imam. Finally, the commentator (Khaiyr al-Ramli) objects to the author's earlier statement that we must follow the Imam without knowing the evidence, pointing out it contradicts the Imam's own saying: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our statement until he knows from where we said it.' The author responds by distinguishing between the Imam's statement (which was for those who could directly see the evidence) and the later position after the madhhab's establishment.

Key Terms
أهلية (ahliyyah): Legal qualification for giving fatwa; having the capacity and readiness to issue rulings.
النظر (al-nazar): The ability to examine and weigh evidence to derive rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a mufti in later times regarding giving fatwa by the Imam's statement?
A) It is only permissible if he knows the evidence.
B) It is obligatory even if he does not know the evidence.
C) It is forbidden unless he has studied all the proofs.
D) It is allowed only for those who have met the Imam.

Key Takeaway
A mufti in the later Hanafi school must give fatwa by Imam Abu Hanifa's statement without necessarily knowing the evidence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
8 min
Ahliyyat al-Nazar wa al-Fatwa: The Two Levels of Mufti Qualification
Defining the qualifications for issuing fatwa and the nature of taqlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ahliyyat al-ijtihad and ahliyyat naql al-fatwa and apply the Hanafi hierarchy for issuing fatwa in contemporary practice.

Core Idea
A mufti today transmits the madhhab's preferred ruling; ijtihad is not required.

This passage clarifies a critical tension in Hanafi ifta: must a mufti know the evidence for every ruling, or is it sufficient to transmit the relied-upon positions of the madhhab? Through the lens of Ibn al-Mubarak's condition and later scholarly resolution, we learn that the qualification for fatwa is layered. The later Hanafi school distinguished between the capacity for ijtihad (ahliyyat al-nazar) and the capacity for transmission (ahliyyat naql al-fatwa). Understanding this distinction is essential for any mufti operating within the madhhab today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial qualification condition
The passage opens with a general principle: a mufti's correct answers must outnumber his mistakes. Find this statement and note the reasoning given (Shari'a is built on the predominant).
This is from al-Walwaljiyyah and sets a baseline.
2
Examine Ibn al-Mubarak's stricter condition
Ibn al-Mubarak required knowledge of hadith, qiyas, and memorization of Abu Hanifa's statements. Note how the author of al-Bahr interprets this as applying only before madhhab codification.
This reveals a historical shift in the role of the mufti.
3
Analyze the objection of Khayr al-Ramli
Al-Khayr al-Ramli objects that al-Bahr's statement contradicts Imam Abu Hanifa's warning. Trace the two responses and understand the resolution: later muftis are narrators, not mujtahids.
The key: 'ما يصدر من غير الأهل ليس بإفتاء حقيقة، وإنما هو حكاية عن المجتهد'.
4
Define the two levels of qualification
Distinguish between ahliyyat al-ijtihad (independent reasoning) and ahliyyat naql al-fatwa (transmission). The passage lists what the latter requires: some ijtihad, knowledge of people's conditions, vigilance against deceit.
This is the mufti's actual role in the later period.
5
Apply the hierarchy to a modern scenario
Consider a mufti today faced with a new financial transaction. He must identify the closest madhhab precedent, verify its tarjih status, and transmit the ruling. He does not derive from primary sources.
This demonstrates the practical functioning of taqlid transmission.

أهلية النظر والفتوى ترجيح بعضها على بعض ، ولا يصير أهلا للفتوى ما لم يصر صوابه أكثر من خطأه ؛ لأن الصواب متى كثر، فقد غلب ولا عبرة في المغلوب بمقابلة الغالب ؛ فإن أمور الشرع مبنيّة على الأعم الأغلب، كذا في "الولوالجية". وفى مناقب الكردري : قال ابن المبارك وقد سئل : " متى يحل للرجل أن يفتى ويلى القضاء؟ قال : إذا كان بصيراً بالحديث والرأي، عارفا بقول أبي حنيفة، حافظا له . وهذا محمول (۱) على إحدى الروايتين عن أصحابنا، و قبل استقرار المذهب، أما بعد التقرر ، فلا حاجة إليه ؛ لأنه يمكنه التقليد اهـ. هذا آخر كلام "البحر " . أقول : ولا يخفى عليك ما في هذا الكلام من عدم الانتظام، ولهذا اعترضه محشيه (۲) الخير الرملي بأن قوله : "يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن لم نعلم من أين قال؟ " مضاد لقول الإمام : " لا يحل لأحد أن يفتى بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا ؟ " ؛ إذ هو صريح في عدم جواز الإفتاء لغير أهل استحضار المسائل والإجابة عنها بالفعل ؛ لأن أهل الشيء من هو متأهل له، ومستعد له استعدادًا قريباً، لا من حصل له ذلك الشيء وحضر عنده بالفعل.
(۱) قوله : "وهذا محمول دفع دخل مقدر تقريره : أن الإمام عبد الله بن المبارك جعل معرفة الحديث والقياس - أى- علم أدلة الأقوال - شرطا لجواز الإفتاء، فعلى هذا لا يجوز الإفتاء من غير معرفة الدليل؟ وهذا خلاف ما ادعاه صاحب البحر من قبل بقوله : "وأما نحن قلنا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن لم نقف على دليله " . وأجاب عنه بجوابين : الأول : اختلف أصحابنا في جواز الإفتاء لمن لم يعرف الدليل وعدم جوازه، وقول عبد الله بن المبارك مبنى على الرواية الثانية . الثاني : ما قاله الإمام ابن المبارك من لزوم معرفة الدليل محمول على ما قبل تدوين المذهب وتنقيحه وتهذيبه، وأما الآن فلا حاجة إلى معرفة الدلائل ثم ترجيح قول غير الإمام لقوة دليله، بل علينا تقليد الإمام، والإفتاء على قوله والقضاء بمذهبه، وإن لم نعلم مأخذه .
(۲) قوله : اعترضه محشيه" أى محشّى "البحر" . (مظ)

أهلية النظر والفتوى الاجتهاد، فكيف يستدل به علی وجوبه؟ فنقول (۱) : ما يصدر من غير الأهل ليس بإفتاء حقيقة، وإنما هو حكاية عن المجتهد أنه قائل بكذا وباعتبار هذا الملحظ تجوز حكاية قول غير الإمام، فكيف يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه؟ ونحن إنما نحكى فتواهم لا غير ، فليتأمل . وتوضيحه : أن المشايخ اطلعوا على دليل الإمام، وعرفوا من أين قال ، واطلعوا على دليل أصحابه، فيرجحون دليل أصحابه على دليله، فيفتون به ولا يظن بهم أنهم عدلوا عن قوله لجهلهم بدليله ؛ فإنا نراهم قد شحنوا كتبهم بنصب الأدلة، ثم يقولون : الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف " مثلا . وحيث لم نكن نحن أهلا للنظر في الدليل، ولم نصل إلى رتبتهم في حصول شرائط التفريع والتأصيل () ، فعلينا حكاية ما يقولونه ؛ لأنهم هم أتباع المذهب الذين نصبوا أنفسهم لتقريره وتحريره (۳) باجتهادهم .
(۲)
وانظر إلى ما قدمناه من قول العلامة قاسم : إن المجتهدين لم يفقدوا حتى نظروا في المختلف، ورجحوا وصححوا . . . إلى أن قال : فعلينا اتباع الراجح والعمل به، كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم " .
(۱) قوله : "فنقول " هذا من تتمة كلام الخير الرملي دفع به ما عسى أن يتوهم : لما لم يجز الإفتاء لغير أهل الاجتهاد فكيف يسوغ إصدار الفتوى لأهل زماننا؟ وتوضيح الدفع: : أن إفتاء غير المجتهد ليس بإفتاء حقيقة، إنما هو نقل كلام المجتهد، ولا يشترط للنقل معرفة الدليل، فهو يحكى ما رجحه المشايخ ، سواء كان قول الإمام أو غيره . قلت : وعلى هذا المفتى في زماننا من اجتمع فيه أهلية نقل الفتوى وإن لم يوجد فيه أهلية الإفتاء، إلا أنه لا بد له من ضرب اجتهاد ومعرفة بأحوال الناس، وذكاء ينظر به في خصوص الوقائع، وتيقظ يتنبه به على مكر الناس واحتيالهم ؛ فهذا كله من أهلية نقل الفتوى
(۲) قوله : "التفريع والتأصيل " أى تخريج الجزئيات وتأسيس القواعد
(۳) قوله : لتقريره وتحريه " أى إثباته بالدلائل وتنقيحه
The qualification of investigation and fatwa: preferring some over others. And one does not become qualified for fatwa unless his correctness becomes more than his error; because when correctness increases, it overcomes, and no consideration is given to the overcome in comparison to the dominant; indeed the matters of the Shari'a are built upon the more general and more prevalent, as in al-Walwaljiyyah. And in Manaqib al-Kardari: Ibn al-Mubarak said when asked, 'When is it permissible for a man to give fatwa and assume judgeship?' He said: 'When he is insightful in hadith and opinion, knowledgeable of the statement of Abu Hanifa, and memorizes it.' And this is carried (1) upon one of the two narrations from our companions, before the establishment of the madhhab. As for after its establishment, there is no need for it; because he can practice taqlid. This is the end of the speech of al-Bahr. I say: It is not hidden from you what is in this speech of lack of order, and for this his commentator (2) al-Khayr al-Ramli objected to it, saying that his statement, 'We must issue fatwa with the statement of the Imam even if we do not know from where he said it?' contradicts the statement of the Imam: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa with our statement until he knows from where we said it.' For it is explicit in the impermissibility of fatwa for other than the people of bringing to mind the issues and answering them actually; because the people of something are those who are qualified for it and ready for it with a near readiness, not those who have attained that thing and it is present with them actually. (1) His statement: 'This is carried' repels an anticipated objection. Its explanation is that Imam Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak made knowledge of hadith and qiyas—i.e., knowledge of the evidences of statements—a condition for the permissibility of fatwa. Thus, according to this, it is not permissible to give fatwa without knowledge of the evidence? This contradicts what the author of al-Bahr previously claimed in his statement: 'As for us, we say we issue fatwa with the statement of the Imam even if we do not come across his evidence.' And he answered with two answers: First, our companions disagreed regarding the permissibility of fatwa for one who does not know the evidence and its impermissibility, and the statement of Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak is based on the second narration. Second, what Imam Ibn al-Mubarak said about the necessity of knowing the evidence is carried upon the period before the codification of the madhhab, its refinement, and its polishing. As for now, there is no need to know the evidences, then to prefer the statement of other than the Imam due to the strength of his evidence; rather we must practice taqlid of the Imam, issue fatwa on his statement, and judge by his madhhab, even if we do not know his source. (2) His statement: 'His commentator objected to it' i.e., the commentator of al-Bahr (Maz). The qualification of investigation and fatwa: ijtihad, so how can it be used as evidence for its obligation? We say (1): What comes from other than the qualified is not actually fatwa; rather it is a narration from the mujtahid that he says such-and-such. And by consideration of this perspective, narrating the statement of other than the Imam is permissible. So how can it be obligatory for us to issue fatwa with the statement of the Imam even if the mashayikh have given fatwa contrary to it? And we only narrate their fatwa, nothing else. So let it be considered. And its clarification is that the mashayikh have come across the evidence of the Imam, and they know from where he said it, and they have come across the evidence of his companions, so they prefer the evidence of his companions over his evidence, and they give fatwa accordingly. And it should not be thought of them that they turned away from his statement due to ignorance of his evidence; for we see that they have filled their books with the establishment of evidences, then they say, 'The fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf,' for example. And since we are not qualified to examine the evidence, and we have not reached their rank in obtaining the conditions of derivation and establishment (2), it is incumbent upon us to narrate what they say; because they are the followers of the madhhab who set themselves to establish and refine it (3) through their ijtihad. (2) And look at what we previously presented from the statement of Allama Qasim: 'The mujtahids are not absent until they looked at what is disputed, and they gave preference and corrected... up to his saying: so it is upon us to follow the preponderant and act upon it, just as if they had given fatwa in their lifetime.' (1) His statement: 'We say' this is from the completion of the speech of al-Khayr al-Ramli, repelling what might be imagined: Since fatwa is not permissible for other than the people of ijtihad, how is issuing fatwa permissible for the people of our time? And the clarification of the repelling: that the fatwa of other than the mujtahid is not actually fatwa; rather it is a transmission of the speech of the mujtahid, and knowledge of the evidence is not required for transmission. So he narrates what the mashayikh have given preference to, whether it is the statement of the Imam or others. I say: And upon this, the mufti in our time is one in whom the qualification of transmitting fatwa is gathered, even if the qualification of issuing fatwa is not present in him. However, he must have a certain amount of ijtihad and knowledge of the conditions of the people, and intelligence by which he looks at particular incidents, and vigilance by which he becomes alert to the deceit and trickery of the people; all this is part of the qualification of transmitting fatwa. (2) His statement: 'derivation and establishment' i.e., deriving particulars and establishing principles. (3) His statement: 'to establish and refine it' i.e., to prove it with evidences and to polish it.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the qualifications required for a mufti and the nature of issuing fatwa in the later period. It begins by stating that a person does not become qualified for fatwa unless his correct answers outnumber his mistakes, because in Shari'a matters the predominant outweighs the less common. This is cited from al-Walwaljiyyah. Then it quotes Ibn al-Mubarak, who required knowledge of hadith, opinion, and memorization of Abu Hanifa's statements for fatwa. The author of al-Bahr commented that this requirement applied before the madhhab was established; after its establishment, taqlid suffices. However, al-Khayr al-Ramli objects that al-Bahr's statement seems to contradict Imam Abu Hanifa's own warning that one should not give fatwa without knowing the source. The resolution is that later muftis are not issuing independent fatwa but are merely transmitting the rulings of the mujtahids. The mashayikh (scholars like Abu Yusuf) had examined the evidences and chosen the preponderant opinion. Therefore, a mufti today must have the qualification of transmission (ahliyyat naql al-fatwa), which includes some understanding of the madhhab, awareness of people's circumstances, and intelligence to apply the correct rulings. The passage clarifies the hierarchical nature of fatwa: only a mujtahid can issue fatwa properly, but later scholars act as transmitters of the madhhab.

Key Terms
أهلية النظر والفتوى (ahliyyat al-nazar wa al-fatwa): The qualification to examine evidence and issue fatwa; i.e., the capacity for ijtihad.
التفريع والتأصيل (al-tafri' wa al-ta'sil): Deriving subsidiary rulings from principles and establishing foundational rules.
تقليد (taqlid): Following the ruling of a mujtahid without knowledge of the evidence.
حكاية (hikaya): Narration or transmission of a ruling without claiming independent authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason a mufti today does not need to know the evidence for every ruling?
A) Because the mashayikh have already performed ijtihad and tarjih, and the mufti transmits their preferred rulings.
B) Because knowledge of evidence is impossible to attain after the first generation.
C) Because Imam Abu Hanifa abolished the requirement.
D) Because the mufti's correctness outnumbers his errors automatically.

Key Takeaway
A mufti in the later Hanafi school is a transmitter of the madhhab's preferred rulings, not an independent mujtahid, but he must still possess some ijtihad to apply rulings to new cases and remain vigilant against deceit.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Two Interpretations of Knowing the Imam's Evidence for Fatwa
Explaining the two meanings of Imam Abu Hanifa's fatwa condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two interpretations of Imam Abu Hanifa's statement on fatwa and identify which strata of muftis each addresses.

Core Idea
Knowing the imam's evidence is obligatory for the mujtahid within the madhhab; for others, it is sufficient to transmit.

Imam Abu Hanifa's famous dictum on fatwa has been understood in two distinct ways. This lesson unpacks both meanings, clarifies who is obligated to know the evidence, and explains why the true mufti is a mujtahid within the madhhab. We will also explore the nature of taqlid and the divisibility of ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations
Read the passage and list the two meanings the author gives for the Imam's statement. Note which part of the passage describes each.
First meaning: mufti must know evidence even for transmitted rulings. Second meaning: mufti must know principles to derive new rulings.
2
Determine the addressee for each meaning
For each interpretation, identify who is being addressed: the mujtahid within the madhhab or the higher strata of muftis (tabaqa 3-5). Explain why the pure muqallid is not included.
The author explicitly states the first addresses the mujtahid fi al-madhhab, the second addresses the third to fifth tabaqat.
3
Analyze the definition of taqlid
Find the definition of taqlid in the passage. Understand why taking a ruling with knowledge of the evidence is not taqlid but a form of ijtihad.
Taqlid is 'taking the statement of another without knowledge of its evidence'.
4
Unpack the objection to the first interpretation
The author notes that the first interpretation is 'far-fetched' (بعيد). Explain why: because the mujtahid within the madhhab is still a muqallid of the absolute mujtahid and not obligated to know evidence. Identify the author's intended response.
The objection is that it would impose an obligation on someone who is not required to know evidence.
5
Apply the concept of tajazzi' al-ijtihad
The passage affirms that ijtihad is divisible. Explain how this allows a scholar to be a mujtahid in some areas (e.g., fara'id) while a muqallid in others. List the scholars who held this view.
This supports the idea that a mufti can know evidence in some matters without being a mujtahid mutlaq.

شرح عقود رسم المفتی الحق أن الاجتهاد يتجزأ يعلم دليل إمامه . ولا شك أنه على هذا خاص بالمفتي المجتهد دون المقلد المحض ؛ فإن التقليد : "هو الأخذ بقول الغير بغير معرفة دليله " . قالوا : فخرج أخذه مع معرفة دليله، فإنه ليس بتقليد ؛ لأنه أخذ من الدليل لا من المجتهد . بل قيل : إن أخذه مع معرفة دليله نتيجة الاجتهاد ؛ لأن معرفة الدليل إنما تكون للمجتهد ؛ لتوقفها على معرفة سلامته من المعارض، وهي متوقفة على استقراء الأدلة كلها، ولا يقدر على ذلك إلا المجتهد . أما مجرد معرفة أن المجتهد الفلاني أخذ الحكم الفلاني من الدليل الفلاني، فلا فائدة فيها . فلابد أن يكون المراد من وجوب معرفة الدليل على المفتى، أن يعرف حاله، حتى يصح له تقليده في ذلك مع الجزم به، وإفتاء غيره به، وهذا لا يتأتى
إلا فى المفتى المجتهد في المذهب، وهو المفتى حقيقة، أما غيره فهو ناقل . لكن كون المراد هذا بعيد (۱) ؛ لأن هذا المفتى حيث لم يكن وصل إلى رتبة الاجتهاد المطلق يلزمه التقليد لمن وصل إليها، ولا يلزمه معرفة دليل إمامه
إلا على قول . قال في "التحرير" : "مسألة : غير المجتهد المطلق يلزمه التقليد وإن كان مجتهداً في بعض مسائل الفقه، أو بعض العلوم كالفرائض، على القول بتجزئ الاجتهاد (۳) وهو الحق (۳)، فيقلد غيره فيما لا يقدر عليه. وقيل
6
(۱) قوله : لكن كون المراد هذا بعيد إشكال على إرادة المجتهد في المذهب من هذا القول تقريره : أن المجتهد في المذهب ومن دونه يلزمه تقليد المجتهد المطلق على قول الجمهور، فهو كغيره من المقلدين والمقلّد لا يلزمه معرفة دليل إمامه ولو كان مجتهداً في بعض المسائل، فحمل قول الإمام على المفتى المجتهد في المذهب لا يصح . وأجاب المصنف عنه بقوله الآتى : لكن نقل الشارح عن الزركشي من الشافعية . . . " بإظهار الفرق بينه وبين غيره من المقلدين العامين، وسنوضحه هناك إن شاء الله تعالى . (۲) قوله : " على القول بتجزئ الاجتهاد" للعلماء في ذلك ثلاثة أقوال : الأول : جواز تجزئة الاجتهاد، وهو قول جمهور العلماء مثل الإمام الغزالي، والآمدى والقرافي، والإمام ابن القيم وابن الهمام، وابن دقيق، وابن السبكي والبهاري
Explanation of the contract of the mufti's code [Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti] 116. The first meaning of their statement: 'It is not permissible for anyone...' In the fatwas of Allamah Ibn al-Shilbi: 'It is not for the judge or the mufti to deviate from the statement of the Imam unless one of the mashayikh explicitly stated that the fatwa is on the statement of someone else. So the judge cannot rule by the statement of someone other than Abu Hanifa in a matter where no other statement has been preferred, and they have preferred the evidence of Abu Hanifa over his evidence; if he rules therein, his ruling is not effective – he has nothing but its nullification.' A section on the meaning of the statement of the imams: 'It is not permissible for anyone to issue a fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said it.' Then know that the statement of the Imam: 'It is not permissible for anyone to issue a fatwa according to our statement... etc.' admits of two meanings (1): One of them: that what is meant is that which is readily understood from it, which is that when a person has established the madhhab of his Imam regarding a ruling, such as the obligation of witr for example, it is not permissible for him to issue a fatwa accordingly until (1) He said: 'It admits of two meanings.' The summary of the first: that the mufti is not permitted to give a fatwa by a statement in the madhhab even if it is explicitly transmitted except after knowing its evidence and its state of strength and weakness. Thus he should not issue a fatwa on the non-validity of marriage contract, for example, in the case of non-compatibility (kafaa) except after knowing its evidence. Accordingly, the addressee of this statement is the mujtahid within the madhhab, because the blind follower (muqallid) is not qualified to know and critique the evidence, so he is not charged with that, and he is allowed to issue fatwa without knowing the evidence if he is qualified to understand the texts and apply them to incidents, as is the condition of most muftis for a long time. Then the author raised a problem regarding this meaning and answered it as will be summarized, God willing. The summary of the second meaning: that whoever intends to give fatwas on matters not explicitly transmitted (ghayr mansusa) by way of derivation (takhrij) based on the principles of the imams of the madhhabs, it is not permissible for him to do so except after knowing the source of the rulings and their origin from which they branched. Accordingly, the addressees are the people of the third, fourth, and fifth strata (tabaqat), and it is not for others to do takhrij; rather, they must transmit the statements of the predecessors, and we must follow what they have transmitted of texts, takhrij, and tarjih. [PAGE_117] 117. Explanation of the contract of the mufti's code. The truth is that ijtihad is divisible; he knows the evidence of his Imam. And there is no doubt that this is specific to the mufti who is a mujtahid, not the pure blind follower (muqallid mahd). For taqlid is: 'taking the statement of another without knowledge of its evidence.' They said: so taking it with knowledge of its evidence is excluded, for it is not taqlid because it is taking from the evidence, not from the mujtahid. Rather, it is said: his taking it with knowledge of its evidence is a result of ijtihad, because knowledge of the evidence is only for the mujtahid, since it depends on knowing its freedom from counter-evidence, and that depends on surveying all the evidences, and only the mujtahid is capable of that. As for mere knowledge that a certain mujtahid derived a certain ruling from a certain evidence, there is no benefit in that. So the intended meaning of the obligation of knowing the evidence upon the mufti must be that he knows its state, so that his taqlid of it is valid with certainty, and his issuing fatwa thereby to others. And this is only achieved for the mufti who is a mujtahid within the madhhab, and he is the true mufti; as for others, they are transmitters (naqil). But that this is intended is far-fetched (1): because this mufti, since he has not reached the level of absolute ijtihad (ijtihad mutlaq), must perform taqlid of those who have reached it, and he is not obligated to know the evidence of his Imam except according to one opinion. He said in al-Tahrir: 'Issue: The non-absolute mujtahid is obliged to perform taqlid even if he is a mujtahid in some matters of fiqh or some sciences like fara'id, according to the view of the divisibility of ijtihad (3), and it is the truth (3), so he follows others in what he is not capable of.' And it was said (6). (1) He said: 'But that this is intended is far-fetched' is an objection to intending the mujtahid within the madhhab from this statement. Its explanation: that the mujtahid within the madhhab and those below him are obliged to perform taqlid of the absolute mujtahid according to the view of the majority, so he is like other blind followers, and the blind follower is not obliged to know the evidence of his Imam even if he is a mujtahid in some matters. So interpreting the Imam's statement to apply to the mufti who is a mujtahid within the madhhab is not valid. And the author answered it by his later statement: 'But the commentator (sharih) transmitted from al-Zarkashi of the Shafi'is...' showing the difference between him and other general blind followers, and we will clarify it there, God willing. (2) He said: 'According to the view of the divisibility of ijtihad.' Scholars have three statements regarding it: the first: the permissibility of the divisibility of ijtihad, and it is the view of the majority of scholars such as Imam al-Ghazali, al-Amidi, al-Qarafi, Imam Ibn al-Qayyim, Ibn al-Humam, Ibn Daqiq, Ibn al-Subki, and al-Bahari.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a methodological commentary on a key rasm rule for muftis: the famous statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, 'It is not permissible for anyone to issue a fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we said it.' The author first cites a fatwa from Ibn al-Shilbi confirming that a judge or mufti should not deviate from the Imam's statement unless a scholar has explicitly stated that the fatwa is on someone else's view. He then introduces a 'mabhas' (section) on the meaning of the imams' statement. The author explains that this statement admits of two interpretations. The first interpretation is the apparent one: a mufti must know the evidence for a ruling even if the ruling is clearly transmitted in the madhhab. For example, if a mufti knows that Imam Abu Hanifa held witr to be wajib, he cannot simply issue a fatwa to that effect without understanding the proof behind it. This interpretation makes the addressee the 'mujtahid fi al-madhhab' (mujtahid within the madhhab), because a pure muqallid (blind follower) is not capable of evaluating evidence. However, the author notes a problem with this interpretation and promises a later answer. The second interpretation is that the statement applies to the derivation of rulings for new cases not explicitly found in the texts (ghayr mansusa). A mufti may not engage in takhrij (analogical derivation) unless he knows the underlying principles and origins from which the rulings branch. This addresses the higher strata of muftis (tabaqa 3, 4, 5), who are capable of takhrij. Those below them must simply transmit the statements of the earlier authorities. The author then affirms that the correct view is that ijtihad is divisible (tajazzi' al-ijtihad). He defines taqlid as 'taking the statement of another without knowledge of its evidence.' Taking a ruling with knowledge of the evidence is not taqlid; it is a form of ijtihad. The true mufti is the one who is a mujtahid within the madhhab; others are mere transmitters. However, he notes that interpreting the Imam's statement as referring to the mujtahid within the madhhab is problematic because such a mufti is still a muqallid of the absolute mujtahid and is not obligated to know the evidence. The author cites al-Tahrir stating that a non-absolute mujtahid must perform taqlid in areas he is not capable of, according to the view that ijtihad is divisible. The passage ends by listing the scholars who held the view of divisibility of ijtihad, including al-Ghazali, al-Amidi, and others.

Key Terms
المفتي (al-mufti): The one who issues fatwas. In this passage, the true mufti is the mujtahid within the madhhab (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab); others are transmitters (naqil).
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar who is capable of deriving rulings within the confines of the Hanafi school, knowing its evidence and principles, but not reaching the level of absolute ijtihad.
التقليد (al-taqlid): Taking the statement of another without knowledge of its evidence.
تجزئ الاجتهاد (tajazzi' al-ijtihad): The view that ijtihad can be partial; a person can be a mujtahid in some areas of fiqh (like fara'id) while being a muqallid in others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first interpretation of Imam Abu Hanifa's statement, who is primarily addressed by the requirement to know the evidence before issuing a fatwa?
A) The pure muqallid who cannot evaluate evidence.
B) The mujtahid within the madhhab (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab).
C) The absolute mujtahid (al-mujtahid al-mutlaq).
D) The common Muslim seeking a fatwa.

Key Takeaway
The true mufti is the mujtahid within the madhhab who knows the evidence; others are transmitters, and the divisibility of ijtihad accommodates different levels of competence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
8 min
The Divisibility of Ijtihad and Its Implication for Muftis
Rule on divisibility of ijtihad for muftis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three views on tajazzu' al-ijtihad and apply the divisibility rule to determine a mufti's obligation to know proofs.

Core Idea
Ijtihad can be partial; a mufti in one specialization need not know proofs from other areas.

This passage tackles a foundational question for muftis: can a scholar be a mujtahid in only some fiqh chapters, or must he master all? The answer determines who qualifies as a mufti and what he must know to issue fatwas. We will explore the definition of taqlid, the three scholarly positions on tajazzu' al-ijtihad, and the practical consequences for muftis today.

Guided Path
1
Define taqlid and its opposite
Identify the precise definition of taqlid given in the text: 'accepting another's statement without knowledge of his proof.' Note that acceptance with proof is not taqlid but following the proof or even a form of ijtihad.
This definition is critical for understanding the mufti's duty.
2
Identify the three views on tajazzu' al-ijtihad
List the three opinions: (1) Permissibility of divisibility (majority), (2) Prohibition (Mulla Khusro, Shawkani), (3) Differentiation (allowed only in inheritance). Understand the reasoning behind each.
The author explicitly supports the first view as 'al-haqq'.
3
Analyze the evidence for the majority view
Examine the proof: many mujtahids answered some questions and not others, yet are accepted as mujtahids. Also, specialization in a single fiqh chapter is possible if one masters its evidences.
Counterargument: if an issue depends on outside evidence, the mujtahid must know that too, but that is part of the chapter's requirements.
4
Apply the rule to a mufti's obligation
Determine: a mufti who is not an absolute mujtahid is a muqallid of the absolute mujtahid, but if ijtihad is divisible, he can be a partial mujtahid and give fatwa in his area of specialization. He must know the proofs for his area, but not for all areas.
This is the key practical implication for the hierarchy of muftis.

Source Text
